Commonwealth v. Clint C.


SJC-07981


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


430 Mass. 219; 715 N.E.2d 1032; 1999 Mass. LEXIS 609


May 7, 1999, Argued  
August 31, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Revised.


PRIOR HISTORY: Suffolk. Indictment found and returned in the Superior Court Department on February 12, 1997. After transfers of the case to the juvenile session of the West Roxbury Division of the District Court Department and then to the Boston Division of the Juvenile Department, the case was heard by Stephen M. Limon, J., on a motion to dismiss. The Supreme Judicial Court granted an application for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth's application for direct appellate review of order of the trial court, Boston Division of the Juvenile Department (Massachusetts), which dismissed a youthful offender indictment under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 119, § 54 (as amended through St. 1996, ch. 200, § 2), charging juvenile with rape of a child.


OVERVIEW: A 15-year-old juvenile was charged with the rape of a child based on a youthful offender indictment under the youthful offender act, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 119, § 54 (as amended through St. 1996, ch. 200, § 2). The juvenile court dismissed the indictment, concluding that the charge of rape of a child did not involve the threat or infliction of serious bodily harm as required by the youthful offender act. On direct appellate review, the court vacated the judgment, because statutory rape was a transferable offense under the youthful offender act. In these circumstances, the invasive nature of the act of penetration, which the Commonwealth would need to prove for rape of a child, created the threat of serious bodily harm.


OUTCOME: Judgment was vacated, because statutory rape was a transferable offense under the youthful offender act. In these circumstances, the invasive nature of the act of penetration, which the Commonwealth would need to prove for rape of a child, created the threat of serious bodily harm.

 

2 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Doe v. Attorney General


SJC-07655


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


430 Mass. 155; 715 N.E.2d 37; 1999 Mass. LEXIS 552


May 7, 1999, Argued  
August 11, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Norfolk. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on November 25, 1996. A motion for a preliminary injunction was heard by Judith A. Cowin, J. The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: A judgment shall enter in the Superior Court declaring that the registration requirements and notification provisions of G. L. c. 6, §§ 178C-178O, are unconstitutional as applied to Doe in the absence of either an individualized hearing to determine whether he is a present threat to children because of the likelihood that he will reoffend or the promulgation of regulations identifying with particularity as to offender and offense the fit between the remedial measure sought by the Commonwealth (registration) and the danger to be averted. An injunction shall be entered in the Superior Court enjoining the Commonwealth from requiring Doe to register under the sex offender act and from distributing or releasing any information concerning him pursuant to that act pending either a determination adverse to him following an individualized hearing before the sex offender board or that board's promulgation of such regulations [***2] and the application of those regulations to him.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed the judgment of the Superior Court Department, Norfolk (Massachusetts), denying his motion for a preliminary injunction regarding the enforcement of the Sex Offender Registration and Notification Act, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 6, §§ 178C-178O.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was a juvenile when he entered into a plea agreement for raping a child. Approximately three years later, plaintiff was served with notice that an application for a complaint had been filed seeking to commence prosecution against him for failing to register as a sex offender. Plaintiff thereupon commenced this action seeking declaratory and injunctive relief. Plaintiff claimed that the Sex Offender Registration and Community Notification Act, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 6, §§ 178C-178O, was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court held that registration and the notification provisions of the sex offender act were unconstitutional as applied to plaintiff in the absence of either an individualized hearing to determine whether plaintiff was a present threat to children or the promulgation of regulations.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the lower court and granted plaintiff's motion for a preliminary injunction enjoining Massachusetts from requiring plaintiff to register under the sex offender act and from distributing or releasing any information concerning him pursuant to that act.

 

3 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Alphas


SJC-07919


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


430 Mass. 8; 712 N.E.2d 575; 1999 Mass. LEXIS 481


March 4, 1999, Argued  
July 7, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Hampden. Complaint received and sworn to in the Palmer Division of the District Court Department on August 10, 1995. A pretrial motion to dismiss was considered by Kenneth J. Cote, Jr., J., and the case was tried before Nancy Dusek-Gomez, J. The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Palmer Division of the District Court Department (Massachusetts) denying defendant's motion to dismiss and convicting defendant of four counts of stalking pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 265, § 43.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of four counts of stalking under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 265, § 43. Defendant appealed and alleged that defendant's pretrial motion to dismiss should have been granted and that the trial court erred by giving improper jury instructions, excluding prior protective orders, and allowing plaintiff prosecutor's cross-examination and closing remarks. Defendant also alleged ineffective assistance of counsel. The court affirmed defendant's convictions and held that there was substantial evidence to convict defendant and any errors did not result in a substantial miscarriage of justice. Defendant was not entitled to dismissal of stalking in violation of a court order because the order in defendant's divorce judgment required defendant not to harass the victim. Erroneous jury instructions did not materially influence the verdict because there was substantial evidence that defendant stalked the victim repeatedly after an amendment to the stalking law. Any potential prejudice from defendant's counsel's conduct or plaintiff's remarks was immaterial based on the substantial evidence against defendant. Evidence of prior protective orders was irrelevant to the charges.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of defendant's motion to dismiss and defendant's convictions for stalking and held that, based on the substantial amount of evidence against defendant, there was not a substantial miscarriage of justice despite errors committed in defendant's trial.

 

4 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Opinion of the Justices to the Senate


SJC-08000


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


429 Mass. 1201; 712 N.E.2d 83; 1999 Mass. LEXIS 488



June 30, 1999, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The Justices answer the question, "No."


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Gloucester city council passed, overriding mayor's veto, a home rule petition that requested the Massachusetts legislature to amend the city charter. The Massachusetts Senate, on consideration of the petition, submitted a question of whether the city council approval over mayor's veto was equivalent to approval by the city council and mayor, as constitutionally required to pass a home rule petition.


OVERVIEW: The city council of Gloucester adopted, over the veto of mayor, a home rule petition addressed to the Massachusetts legislature requesting the enactment of a special act changing the city charter. Under Ma. Const. art. 89, § 8, cl. 1, there were three methods by which a city could petition the legislature to enact legislation that affected only that city. First, by petition filed or approved by the voters of a city. Second, by petition filed by a mayor and city council; and third, by petition from the town meeting of a town. The Massachusetts Senate, upon reviewing the bill, submitted a question to the court as to whether the city council's override of mayor's veto of a home rule petition constituted approval by a mayor and the city council of that city. The court held that where state constitution gave directions respecting the times or modes of proceeding in which a power should be exercised, there was at least a strong presumption that it should be exercised in that time and mode only. Accordingly, the court answered that where approval by both mayor and city council was required to approve an action, the approval of both was required, not just one or the other.


OUTCOME: The court, in response to the question submitted by the Massachusetts Senate, determined that the city council's override of mayor's veto of a home rule petition did not satisfy the constitutional requirement that the petition be approved by mayor and the city council.

 

5 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Keita


SJC-07922


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


429 Mass. 843; 712 N.E.2d 65; 1999 Mass. LEXIS 403


March 5, 1999, Argued  
June 29, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Norfolk. Complaint received and sworn to in the Quincy Division of the District Court Department on November 22, 1996. The case was heard by Paul F. X. Moriarty, J. After review by the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court granted leave to obtain further appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sought further review of an order of the Court of Appeals (Massachusetts), reversing defendant's criminal conviction for indecent assault and battery, because defendant lacked criminal responsibility. Plaintiff asserted that there was sufficient evidence of presumption of sanity presented to the trial court to warrant the finding of defendant's guilt beyond a reasonable doubt.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted on a charge of indecent assault and battery, in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 265, § 13H. Defendant raised insanity as a defense and offered testimony of an expert witness who gave an opinion on defendant's mental condition as mentally ill. Upon a jury-waived trial, defendant was found guilty. Defendant appealed the conviction, which was reversed by reason of defendant's lack of criminal responsibility. Plaintiff sought further appellate review, which was granted. The court reversed judgment in favor of plaintiff and held that the evidence, including defendant's disposition at the time of arrest, his ability to answer questions during booking, and his cooperative nature, all warranted a finding of proof beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was criminally responsible at the time of the crime. Further, the court held that it would continue to require the burden of proof of sanity be placed on plaintiff, rather than placing a burden of lack of criminal responsibility on defendant. The court held that precedent, and lack of controlling legislation, influenced the court's decision not to shift the burden of proof of insanity to defendant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed judgment in favor of plaintiff, and upheld defendant's conviction for indecent assault and battery. The court held that the evidence, including defendant's disposition at the time of arrest, his ability to answer questions during booking, and his cooperative nature, all warranted a finding of proof beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was criminally responsible at the time of the crime.

 

6 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Valliere v. Superintendent


SJC-07566


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


429 Mass. 1024; 711 N.E.2d 587; 1999 Mass. LEXIS 396



June 23, 1999, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed from a single justice's denial of his petition for habeas corpus relief. Petitioner argued that the court did not have authority to resentence him to life imprisonment after the U.S. Supreme Court invalidated the type of procedure under which petitioner had been sentenced to death, because such authority rested only with the jury.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted, by jury, of murder and armed robbery. The jury recommended the death penalty. Thereafter, the U.S. Supreme Court invalidated the type of procedure under which petitioner was sentenced. On appeal, the court affirmed the convictions, but vacated the death sentences and remanded for resentencing to life imprisonment. Petitioner filed a petition for habeas corpus relief, contending that the court had no authority to resentence him to life imprisonment, because it was the jury, not the court, which had the power to recommend a life sentence in place of execution. A single justice denied the petition, and the appellate court affirmed. The court found petitioner's claims were not based on grounds distinct from the issues at the indictment, trial, conviction, or sentencing. Furthermore, petitioner opposed a matter of sentencing. As such, a petition for habeas corpus would not lie, because petitioner was not entitled to immediate release. The court found that the most petitioner was entitled to was resentencing, not release. The court held that by changing the death sentence to life imprisonment, the court did not infringe on any rights belonging to petitioner.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed denial of a petition for habeas corpus relief. The court held that, by changing petitioner's death sentence to life imprisonment after the U.S. Supreme Court invalidated the type of procedure under which petitioner had been sentenced to death, the court did not infringe on any rights belonging to petitioner. The court found that the most petitioner would be entitled to was resentencing, not release.

 

7 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Murphy v. Department of Correction


SJC-07979


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


429 Mass. 736; 711 N.E.2d 149; 1999 Mass. LEXIS 366



June 18, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Middlesex. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on December 19, 1997. The case was heard by James F. McHugh, III, J. The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgment vacated. Case remanded to the Superior Court for the entry of a declaration that St. 1997, c. 106, § 8, applies by its terms to the plaintiff.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth appealed a declaratory judgment entered by the Superior Court Department of Middlesex, Massachusetts, in favor of plaintiff in plaintiff's action seeking a judgment that he was not required, under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 22E (1997), to submit a deoxyribonucleic acid (DNA) sample for inclusion in the State DNA database. The Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, on its own initiative, transferred the case from the Appeals Court.


OVERVIEW: Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 22E (1997) created a state deoxyribonucleic acid (DNA) database of individuals convicted of certain offenses. The plaintiff was convicted in 1985 of an offense listed in the statute. He completed his sentence and was released in 1993. He was later convicted of another offense, which was not on the list. He remained incarcerated for that offense on the effective date of the statute. The Department of Correction informed the plaintiff that he would be required to submit a DNA sample because he had been previously convicted of a listed offense and was incarcerated on the statute's effective date. The plaintiff sought and was awarded a judgment declaring that the statute did not require him to submit the sample, alleging that the statute applied only to those who were incarcerated for a listed offense on the effective date. On appeal, the court vacated the judgment and remanded the case for entry of a declaration that the statute, by its terms, applied to the plaintiff. The court adopted the construction that the statute applied to anyone incarcerated on or after the statute's effective date who had ever been convicted of a listed offense.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment for plaintiff and remanded the case for entry of a declaration that the state statute, by its terms, required plaintiff to submit a deoxyribonucleic acid sample. The court adopted the construction that the statute applied to anyone incarcerated on or after the statute's effective date who had ever been convicted of a listed offense.

 

8 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Chebacco Liquor Mart v. Alcoholic Bevs. Control Comm'n


SJC-07907


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


429 Mass. 721; 711 N.E.2d 135; 1999 Mass. LEXIS 365


April 9, 1999, Argued  
June 16, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Alcoholic Liquors, Sunday closing law. Common Day of Rest. Constitutional Law, Equal protection of laws. Due Process of Law, Sunday closing law. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on June 27, 1997. The case was heard by Margaret R. Hinkle, J. The Supreme Judicial Court granted an application for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Superior Court reversed and judgment shall be entered for the commission.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Alcoholic Beverages Control Commission appealed the judgment of the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts), which reversed commission's decision that held plaintiff had made Sunday sales, in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 138, § 14 and Mass. Regs. Code tit. 204, § 2.05(2) (1993), and suspended plaintiff's license for 30 days. Plaintiff's application for direct appellate review was granted.


OVERVIEW: Defendant Alcoholic Beverages Control Commission suspended plaintiff package store's license after finding that plaintiff had sold alcoholic beverages in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 138, § 14, and Mass. Regs. Code tit. 204, § 2.05(2) (1993). That decision was reversed on judicial review on the ground that Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 136, § 6(52), which provided an exception to the Sunday sales prohibition for municipalities located within ten miles of the New Hampshire or Vermont border, violated state and federal principles of equal protection and due process. Defendant appealed, and plaintiff's application for direct appellate review was granted. On appeal, the court reversed and entered judgment in defendant's favor. Plaintiff did not claim that it was a member of a suspect group or that a fundamental interest was involved. Also, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 136, § 6(52) served the legitimate purposes of capturing tax revenue, retaining business that otherwise would have been lost to the bordering states, and promoting the public convenience, and it was rationally related to achieving those purposes. Thus, the statute did not violate plaintiff's equal protection or due process rights.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's decision and entered judgment in defendant commission's favor. Plaintiff store's equal protection and due process rights were not violated by the statutory exception to the Sunday closing law, for the statutory exception was rationally related to achieving permissible legislative objectives, and plaintiff failed to claim that it was a member of a suspect class or that a fundamental interest was involved.

 

9 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Gonsalves


SJC-07962


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


429 Mass. 658; 711 N.E.2d 108; 1999 Mass. LEXIS 381


April 5, 1999, Argued  
June 14, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Plymouth. Indictment found and returned in the Superior Court Department on May 27, 1997. A pretrial motion to suppress evidence was heard by Patrick F. Brady, J. An application for an interlocutory appeal was allowed by Greaney, J., in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk and the appeal was reported to the Appeals Court by him. After review by the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court granted leave to obtain further review.



DISPOSITION: Order allowing motion to suppress affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth of Massachusetts applied for further appellate review, after affirmance by the Appeals Court for the County of Suffolk (Massachusetts), of the Superior Court's decision to suppress evidence against defendant, who was indicted for trafficking in cocaine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a passenger in a taxicab that was stopped by a state trooper for driving erratically, was ordered out of the taxi by the trooper, who then found cocaine on the seat. Defendant moved to suppress the evidence before his trial for drug trafficking. The court allowed the motion to suppress because the trooper had no objective basis upon which to order defendant out of the vehicle. The appeals court affirmed the suppression order, concluding that the trooper had no reasonable basis to support his order to the defendant to step out of the taxicab. The prosecution was granted further review and urged the court to adopt the United States Supreme Court rule holding that a police officer does not violate the U.S. Const. amend. IV when, in a routine traffic stop, he orders a passenger out of the vehicle. The court declined, holding that Mass. Const. art. 14 required that a police officer, in a routine traffic stop, must have had a reasonable belief that the officer's safety, or the safety of others, was in danger before ordering a driver out of a motor vehicle. The decision suppressing the evidence was upheld.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order allowing the motion to suppress was affirmed because the trooper had no reasonable basis to support his order to defendant to step out of the taxicab

 

10 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Prudential Ins. Co. of Am. v. Comm'r of Revenue


SJC-07841


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


429 Mass. 560; 709 N.E.2d 1096; 1999 Mass. LEXIS 212


February 4, 1999, Argued  
May 10, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Appeal from a decision of the Appellate Tax Board. The Supreme Judicial Court granted an application for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Decision of the Appellate Tax Board affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed from the decision of the Appellate Tax Board (Massachusetts) in favor of defendant, which found that the separate treatment of plaintiff's life insurance premiums and health and accident premiums for retaliatory tax purposes was required by statute and did not violate the constitution.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, a New Jersey corporation that collected premiums on both life insurance and health and accident insurance in Massachusetts during the 1990 and 1991 tax years, appealed the decision of the Appellate Tax Board (Board) that was adverse to plaintiff. The issue was whether it was lawful for Massachusetts to calculate retaliatory taxes on the insurance premiums of a foreign insurer separately for life insurance premiums and for premiums on all other lines of insurance. The supreme judicial court affirmed the decision of the Board that the separate treatment of plaintiff's life insurance premiums and health and accident premiums for retaliatory tax purposes was required by statute and did not violate the equal protection provisions of the state and federal constitutions.


OUTCOME: The decision of the Appellate Tax Board for defendant was affirmed because the separate treatment of plaintiff's life insurance premiums and health and accident premiums for retaliatory tax purposes was required by statute, and did not violate plaintiff's constitutional right to equal protection.

 

11 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Florence F.


SJC-07958


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


429 Mass. 523; 709 N.E.2d 418; 1999 Mass. LEXIS 204


April 5, 1999, Argued  
May 5, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Bristol. Complaint for contempt filed in the Taunton Division of the Juvenile Court Department on April 4, 1997. After transfer of the matter to the Fall River Division, a motion to dismiss was heard by John P. Corbett, J. The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: State appealed from a judgment of the Fall River Juvenile Court (Massachusetts) that granted defendant juvenile's motion to dismiss a criminal contempt complaint filed against her after she failed to attend school as ordered by the Juvenile Court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant juvenile was directly ordered by the Juvenile Court during a Children in Need of Services proceeding to attend school. After she failed to do so, her probation officer filed a criminal complaint to find her in contempt. Defendant's motion to dismiss was granted, and the state appealed. The court affirmed. The court held that Juvenile Courts lacked the authority to issue direct orders against juveniles except when as a condition of custody. For criminal contempt to issue, the underlying order had to be valid. Because the order directing defendant to attend school was beyond the scope of the Juvenile Court's authority, the order was not valid; therefore, defendant could not be charged with criminal contempt.


OUTCOME: Judgment granting defendant juvenile's motion to dismiss a complaint charging her with criminal contempt of a Juvenile Court order directing her to attend school was affirmed because the Juvenile Court lacked the power to issue such direct orders during Children in Need of Services proceedings. Without a valid order, no contempt complaint could be filed.

 

12 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Ellis


SJC-07846


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


429 Mass. 362; 708 N.E.2d 644; 1999 Mass. LEXIS 139


January 4, 1999, Argued  
April 14, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Worcester. Indictment. Indictments found and returned in the Superior Court Department, forty-two on March 18, 1997, and sixty-three on September 12, 1997, respectively. A motion to dismiss was heard by Robert H. Bohn, Jr., J., and an alternative motion to report questions of law to the Appeals Court was heard by him. The Supreme Judicial Court granted an application for direct appellate review.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, including attorneys, staff, and clients of a law firm, moved in the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts) to dismiss indictments against them after they were charged with insurance fraud and prosecuted by the insurance fraud division of the state attorney general's office. The motion was denied and the matter was forwarded via applications for direct appellate review. Defendant asserted constitutional due process violations.


OVERVIEW: Defendants, including attorneys, staff, and clients of a law firm, moved to dismiss insurance fraud indictments that were prosecuted by the insurance fraud division of the state attorney general's (AG) office. The motion was denied and the matter was forwarded via applications for direct appellate review. Defendants claimed that the statutorily prescribed funding scheme for insurance company underwriting of investigations and prosecutions conducted by the insurance fraud division of the AG's office, found in 1996 Mass. Acts ch. 427, § 13, was unconstitutional and violated due process. Specifically, defendants asserted that the AG's office was not disinterested because it relied upon insurance companies for funding. On review, the appellate court determined that there was the possibility of improper influence by private interests on the exercise of prosecutorial discretion because of the closeness of the AG to the private interest groups. However, the court concluded that defendants had not demonstrated that their constitutional rights had been violated by the statutory pattern where they failed to show bias. Therefore, the order was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The order which denied defendants' motion to dismiss was affirmed because, although the appearance of impropriety may have existed where insurance companies funded the insurance fraud division of the state attorney general's office, defendants were unable to demonstrate that their constitutional rights had been violated.

 

13 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. King


SJC-07862


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


429 Mass. 169; 706 N.E.2d 685; 1999 Mass. LEXIS 115


February 1, 1999, Argued  
March 5, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended.


PRIOR HISTORY: Berkshire. Complaint received and sworn to in the Pittsfield Division of the District Court Department on April 7, 1995. A motion to dismiss was heard by Fredric D. Rutberg, J. The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Case remanded to District Court for determination whether evidence of defendant's intoxication was overwhelming or whether other factors rendered the violation harmless in the circumstances.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth appealed a judgment from the Pittsfield Division of the District Court Department (Massachusetts), which granted defendant's motion to dismiss the charge against him of driving while under the influence of alcohol on the grounds that defendant's right to an independent medical examination under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 263, § 5A was violated.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was arrested past midnight for driving while under the influence of alcohol, he told police that he wanted to exercise his right under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 263, § 5A to an independent medical examination. He was not able to exercise that right, however, because the bail magistrate refused to hold a bail hearing at that time of night. Defendant thereafter successfully moved to dismiss the complaint, alleging a deprivation of his right to a prompt bail hearing and of his right to an independent medical examination. The court held that the violation of defendant's § 5A right was prima facie evidence that he was prejudiced in that his opportunity to obtain and present potentially exculpatory evidence had been restricted or destroyed. This presumption of prejudice, however, could be overcome by overwhelming evidence of intoxication or by other evidence indicating that the omission was not prejudicial in the circumstances. Thus, the case was remanded for a determination of whether the evidence of defendant's intoxication was overwhelming or whether other factors rendered the violation harmless under the circumstances.


OUTCOME: Although defendant was presumed to be prejudiced by the violation of his right to an independent medical examination upon his arrest for driving while under the influence of alcohol, the court remanded the case for a determination of whether the evidence of defendant's intoxication was overwhelming or whether other factors rendered the violation of his right to an independent medical examination harmless under the circumstances.

 

14 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Nashoba Communs. Ltd. Pshp. v. Board of Assessors


SJC-07863


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


429 Mass. 126; 706 N.E.2d 653; 1999 Mass. LEXIS 112


January 7, 1999, Argued  
March 4, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Appeal from a decision of the Appellate Tax Board. The Supreme Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order from the Appellate Tax Board (Board) (Massachusetts), in which the Board held that appellant's personal property was exempt from taxation under Mass. Gen. Law ch. 59, § 18.


OVERVIEW: Appellant filed an application for abatement of personal property tax, claiming that its cable and other electronic equipment located over public ways, property for which it was assessed, was exempt from taxation. The Appellate Tax Board (Board) denied the application and the appeal ensued. The supreme court affirmed the Board's decision holding that Mass. Gen. Law ch. 59, § 18 (5) made no provision for the taxation of poles with the wires thereon erected on public ways. According to the supreme court, Mass. Gen. Law ch. 59, § 18 (5) specifically pertained to partnerships and no provision was made exempting the personal property appellant sought to have exempted. The supreme court held that appellant could not use the provision applicable to corporations to attempt to exempt the personal property. The supreme court also rejected appellant's assertion that the provision was unconstitutional. The supreme court held that the classification was not violative of the equal protection clause because the distinction upon which it rested had a fair and rational relation to the object sought to be accomplished by the enactment.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the judgment holding that appellant's personal property was not exempt from taxation because the statute specifically provided that cable and other electronic equipment located over public ways belonging to a partnership was not exempt from taxation.

 

15 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Greater Boston Real Estate Bd. v. City of Boston


SJC-07687


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


428 Mass. 797; 705 N.E.2d 256; 1999 Mass. LEXIS 23


November 2, 1998, Argued  
February 5, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended.


PRIOR HISTORY: Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the City of Boston Division of the Housing Court Department on June 4, 1996. The case was heard by E. George Daher, J., on motions for summary judgment. The Supreme Judicial Court granted an application for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Judge's decision affirmed that (1) ordinance is outside the scope of the enabling act; and (2) severability provision in § 8 cannot salvage the remainder of the ordinance.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city appealed a judgment from the City of Boston Division of the Suffolk Housing Court Department (Massachusetts), which granted plaintiff real estate board's motion for summary judgment in plaintiff's action seeking a declaration that defendant's ordinance, Boston, Mass., Ordinances ch. 3 (1996), was invalid on the ground that it exceeded the authority vested in defendant by the enabling statute, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 527 (1983).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff real estate board brought an action seeking a declaration that defendant city's ordinance, Boston, Mass., Ordinances ch. 3 (1996) (the ordinance), was invalid. The trial court granted plaintiff's motion for summary judgment and struck down the entire ordinance, holding that it exceeded the authority granted to defendant by the enabling act, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 527 (1983) (the enabling act). The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court determined that the definition of "tenant" contained in the ordinance was overly broad because the ordinance applied to tenants taking occupancy after there had been a conversion to condominiums or cooperative. The enabling act authorized protection of tenants from the hardships associated with condominium conversion, not protection of tenants who moved into a unit long after it had become a condominium unit. Further, the invalid elements of the ordinance were too entwined with the rest of the ordinance to permit the court to excise them and to enforce the remainder of the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed summary judgment in favor of plaintiff real estate board in plaintiff's action seeking a declaration that defendant city's ordinance was invalid. The ordinance, which provided protection for tenants involved in condominium conversions, was facially invalid where it exceeded the authority granted by the enabling statute because it afforded protection to tenants who took occupancy after the conversion.

 

16 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Massachusetts Eye & Ear Infirmary v. Commissioner of the Div. of Med. Assistance


SJC-07735


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


428 Mass. 805; 705 N.E.2d 592; 1999 Mass. LEXIS 25


November 2, 1998, Argued  
February 5, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended.


PRIOR HISTORY: Suffolk. Civil actions commenced in the Superior Court Department on August 31, 1995, and September 25, 1995. The cases were heard by Patrick J. King, J., on motions for summary judgment, and a motion to amend judgments was heard by him. The Supreme Judicial Court granted an application for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant medical assistance agency appealed an amended judgment from the Superior Court (Massachusetts), which concluded that it wrongfully denied under its prepayment review program all reimbursement to plaintiff hospitals for services provided to several Medicaid patients on the grounds that they did not require inpatient hospital care and which ordered that defendant reimburse plaintiffs at the outpatient rate upon such determination.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed an amended judgment that concluded that defendant medical assistance agency wrongfully denied plaintiff hospitals all reimbursement for medical services provided to several Medicaid patients because they did not require inpatient hospital care and which ordered defendant to reimburse plaintiffs at the outpatient rate upon such determination. The manner in which defendant evaluated medical necessity for inpatient services under its prepayment review program was not defined in any meaningful way in the implementing regulations and conflicted with federal Medicaid statutes that mandated that defendant's utilization review standards assure that payments are consistent with efficiency, economy, and quality of care. Rather, defendant's program considered the appropriateness of plaintiffs' medical services on a case-by-case basis based on a retrospective evaluation of the patients' ailments and outcome, and then imposed a severe all-or-nothing penalty for treatment in the wrong setting. Since defendant failed to take into account the risk to the patient as assessed by the physician at the time of admission, defendant's administrative action was arbitrary and capricious.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment concluding that defendant medical assistance agency wrongfully denied plaintiff hospitals reimbursement for services provided to Medicaid patients and ordered defendant to pay the outpatient rate because defendant's action under a prepayment review program was arbitrary and capricious where relevant terms were not meaningfully defined and conflicted with federal statutes.

 

17 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


DiBiase v. Commissioner of Ins.


SJC-07754


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


428 Mass. 755; 704 N.E.2d 1188; 1999 Mass. LEXIS 18


November 6, 1998, Argued  
February 1, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on August 30, 1996. The case was heard by Nonnie S. Burnes, J., on a motion for partial summary judgment. The Supreme Judicial Court granted an application for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff policyholder appealed a judgment from the Suffolk Superior Court Department (Massachusetts), which entered summary judgment in favor of defendants, insurance commissioner and insurance company, in plaintiff's action claiming civil rights violations as the result of the demutualization of a savings bank life insurance system. Summary judgment was granted on the ground that the action was not commenced within the statute of limitations.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff policyholder brought an action against defendants, state insurance commissioner and state savings bank life insurance company, alleging that her rights had been violated by certain actions taken in the demutualization of the savings bank life insurance system under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 499, § 23. Plaintiff claimed that her contract rights had been impaired in violation of the state and federal constitutions, that her property had been taken in violation of her constitutional rights to due process of law, and that defendants violated 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The appellate court affirmed the judgment of the lower court, which granted summary judgment in favor of defendants on the ground that plaintiff's claims were barred by the statute of limitations prescribed by Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 260, § 2A. The court agreed that plaintiff's claims were barred by the three-year statute of limitations. Further, the court held that plaintiff's rights to procedural due process were not violated because she received constructive notice of the enactment of the legislation, and she also received personal notice in the form of a letter from defendant insurance company.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed summary judgment in favor of defendants, state insurance commissioner and state savings bank life insurance system, in plaintiff policyholder's action claiming violation of her civil rights by the demutualization of the insurance system. Plaintiff's claims were barred by statute of limitations, and plaintiff's due process rights were not violated because she received constructive notice of the enactment of the legislation.

 

18 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


A.F.M., Ltd. v. City of Medford


SJC-07714


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


428 Mass. 1020; 704 N.E.2d 184; 1999 Mass. LEXIS 7



January 14, 1999, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Grant of the preliminary injunction is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city and city council challenged an order from the superior court (Massachusetts) that granted plaintiff corporation a preliminary injunction enjoining defendants from enforcing Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 181, §§ 4, 9 or Medford Zoning Ordinances ch. 29, §§ 5.3, 16A against plaintiff's application for a special permit for its proposed operation of a retail store for adult books and videos within 750 feet of a residential district.


OVERVIEW: Defendant city and city council appealed the trial court's order that preliminarily enjoined defendants from enforcing Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 181, §§ 4, 9 or Medford Zoning Ordinances ch. 29, §§ 5.3, 16A against plaintiff's application for a special permit to operate an adult bookstore within 750 feet of a residential district. On appeal, the court affirmed the order that granted the injunction. The court first noted that the trial court properly determined that the zoning scheme confined adult businesses to 0.11 percent of defendant city's total developable land and that defendant city was obligated, as a practical matter, to ensure that its regulatory scheme did not unreasonably foreclose avenues for communication of the material plaintiff intended to sell. The court ruled, therefore, that the preliminary injunction was properly entered because defendant city failed to show that plaintiff had been left with reasonable alternative means of communication and because defendant city did not present any information explaining why it was reasonable to restrict adult businesses to such a minuscule portion of the developable land in the city.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an order that preliminarily enjoined defendants from enforcing state statutes and local zoning ordinances against plaintiff's adult bookstore. Because defendant city did not show that plaintiff had been left with reasonable alternative means of communication and did not present any information as to why it was reasonable to restrict adult businesses to a small portion of developable land, the injunction was properly issued.

 

19 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Opinion of the Justices to the House of Representatives


SJC-07851


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


428 Mass. 1201; 702 N.E.2d 8; 1998 Mass. LEXIS 693



November 19, 1998, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Question 2 answered in the affirmative. Unnecessary to consider Questions 1 and 3.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The House of Representatives of the Commonwealth of Massachusetts asked the court to consider a proposed statute in an advisory opinion. The court was asked to respond to three questions regarding the constitutionality of Section 2 of H.R. 5822 (Mass. 1998), which proposed a reduction in the surcharge on vehicular rental transaction contracts for city residents.


OVERVIEW: The House of Representatives of the Commonwealth of Massachusetts requested that the court issue an advisory opinion as to whether the enactment of Section 2 of H.R. 5822 (Mass. 1998), in reducing a city's surcharge on vehicular rental transaction contracts for city residents, would violate the Commerce Clause of the U.S. Constitution. U.S. Const. art. I, § 8. The court determined that the bill proposed a facially discriminatory tax that violated the commerce clause because it plainly imposed a different burden on vehicle renters who were nonresidents than on those vehicle renters who were city residents. The rental of vehicles in the city was an aspect of interstate transportation because many renters were interstate travelers who affected interstate commerce regardless of whether they traveled as tourists or for business purposes. To the extent that vehicles were rented for commercial use, the proposed measure discriminated against out-of-state businesses as well as nonresidents. The local purposes of funding a convention center and reducing permanent ownership of motor vehicles by city residents were better pursued by taxes that did not discriminate on the basis of residency.


OUTCOME: In an advisory opinion, the court determined that the surcharge proposed by Section 2 of H.R. 5822 (Mass. 1998), discriminated against interstate commerce, contravened the dormant aspect of the Commerce Clause of the U.S. Constitution, and was invalid. The court declined to address whether the bill violated the Privileges and Immunities Clause and the Equal Protection Clause of the U.S. Constitution or the Massachusetts Declaration of Rights.

 

20 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Pike


SJC-07806


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


428 Mass. 393; 701 N.E.2d 951; 1998 Mass. LEXIS 691


October 5, 1998, Argued  
November 19, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Hampden. Indictments found and returned in the Superior Court Department on October 24, 1996. The cases were tried before William H. Welch, J. The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed but case remanded to the Superior Court for resentencing in accordance with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts), which convicted defendant for the unauthorized use of a motor vehicle and assault and battery by means of a dangerous weapon. Defendant received a two year suspended sentence and a probation condition barring him from entering the state.


OVERVIEW: The trial court rendered a judgment convicting defendant for the unauthorized use of a motor vehicle and assault and battery by means of a dangerous weapon. Defendant also received a two year suspended sentence and a probation condition barring him from entering the state. On appeal, the court found the trial court did not err in not instructing the jury on self-defense. The evidence did not support a finding that he was justified in throwing a radio at the victim, even though he may have been justified in grabbing or striking the victim in the first stage of the fight. Further, there was no evidence that defendant attempted to avoid further physical contact or that he was unable to do so. Also, defendant was not entitled to a jury instruction on the defense of necessity for taking the motor vehicle. There was no evidence that danger was imminent, and no evidence that there were no lawful alternatives available. The court affirmed defendant's convictions, but remanded for resentencing. The probation condition banishing him from the state was invalid because it was not reasonably related to the goals of sentencing and probation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which convicted defendant for the unauthorized use of a motor vehicle, and assault and battery by means of a dangerous weapon because there were no errors in not allowing a jury instruction on self-defense and necessity. The court remanded for resentencing because the probation condition barring defendant from entering the state was invalid.

 

21 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


White v. City of Boston


SJC-07652


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


428 Mass. 250; 700 N.E.2d 526; 1998 Mass. LEXIS 536


September 10, 1998, Argued  
October 16, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on November 24, 1995. The case was heard by Thayer Fremont-Smith, J., on motions for summary judgment, and entry of separate and final judgment was ordered by Charles M. Grabau, J. The Supreme Judicial Court granted an application for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Summary judgment for plaintiff affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The plaintiff ex-police officer filed a complaint in the Superior Court Department, Suffolk (Massachusetts) against the defendant City challenging the city's denial of his reinstatement. Both parties filed motions for summary judgment. The court allowed the plaintiff's motion for summary judgment on the Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 32, § 8, claim and ordered the defendants to reinstate him. The City appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that the legislature removed all discretionary language when it amended § 8 (2). It clearly demonstrated its intent to direct automatic reinstatement of a formerly disabled, but now capable, employee by replacing the operative language of "may, with the approval of the head of any department" with "shall." Both parties acknowledged that the legislation was enacted soon after publication of a local media investigation concerning medical retirees. News articles profiled retirees who appeared to be profiting simultaneously from their disability pensions and from private careers, even though some of their private pursuits involved physical demands equal to, or greater than, those that had been imposed on them in their civil service positions. Employee was entitled to reinstatement. The court also declined to hold § 8 (2) unconstitutional according to the City's argument, as it created an absolute preference in favor of disability retirees, thus violating Mass. Const. Decl. Rights art. 6 and 7. Case-by-case evaluations were conducted of each individual employee and only after the medical panel evaluated the employee would reinstatement have been ordered.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment for plaintiff affirmed.

 

22 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Doe v. Sex Offender Registry Bd.


SJC-07608


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


428 Mass. 90; 697 N.E.2d 512; 1998 Mass. LEXIS 464


February 2, 1998, Argued  
July 24, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Revised.


PRIOR HISTORY: Middlesex. Civil actions commenced in the Superior Court Department on January 31, 1997, and February 4, 1997, respectively. Questions of law were reported to the Appeals Court by Margot Botsford, J., and Lawrence B. Wernick, J., where the appeals were consolidated. The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct review.



DISPOSITION: Reported rulings vacated and direct the entry of judgments vacating board classifications and remanding matters to board of classification hearings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated appeal, defendant Sex Offender Registry Board appealed orders entered by the Superior Court (Massachusetts) in which plaintiff sex offenders were awarded a judicial evidentiary hearing before classification under the Sex Offender Registration and Community Notification Act, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 6, § 178C-O, and in which portions of the act were deemed invalid on procedural due process grounds.


OVERVIEW: Three sex offenders were assigned risk classifications by the board without a hearing. The sex offenders filed judicial appeals under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 6, § 178M. The trial courts invalidated portions of the act and required judicial evidentiary hearings. The court agreed that an evidentiary hearing was required on the appropriateness of the risk classifications. However, the court determined that the hearing was required to be conducted by the board. To satisfy constitutional due process, the board was required to show by a preponderance of evidence that it had properly classified the sex offenders and that close attention was given to the evidence; detailed findings were required. Because the sex offenders had a privacy interest in avoiding registration, but did not face a potential loss of liberty or a stigma as great as that flowing from a criminal conviction, a higher standard of proof was not warranted. The preponderance of the evidence standard did not create an unusual risk of an erroneous classification and a higher standard of proof would have been unduly burdensome and inconsistent with the goal of protecting the public from recidivistic sex offenders.


OUTCOME: The orders requiring an evidentiary hearing before the trial courts and invalidating portions of the Sex Offender Registration Act were vacated, and the sex offenders' classifications were vacated. The cases were remanded to the board for evidentiary hearings at which the burden would be on the board to show the propriety of the classifications by a preponderance of the evidence and to make specific fact findings supporting its classifications.

 

23 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Dimino v. Secretary of the Commonwealth


SJC-07685


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


427 Mass. 704; 695 N.E.2d 659; 1998 Mass. LEXIS 332


April 10, 1998, Argued  
June 23, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on December 18, 1997. The case was reported by Fried, J.



DISPOSITION: Case remanded to the county court for entry of judgment declaring that Attorney General's certification of the initiative was improper.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, voters and business associations, filed a declaratory judgment action in the Supreme Judicial Court for the County of Suffolk (Massachusetts), which challenged the decision of defendant attorney general, who had certified that an initiative petition did not conflict with Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights amend. art. 48, Part II, § 3. Defendant secretary of state was also a party to the action.


OVERVIEW: The Massachusetts Turnpike Authority was financed by bonds that were paid off by tolls that were collected on the turnpike. Trust agreements gave the bondholders a security interest in the revenues that were generated by the tolls. The backers of an initiative proposed to reduce, then eliminate, the tolls on the roads managed by the Turnpike Authority. The attorney general certified that the initiative petition did not concern matters excluded from the initiative process under Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights amend. art. 48, Part II, § 3. The court overturned the attorney general's certification and ordered the county court to enter judgment declaring that the certification was improper. The court held that the bondholders' security interest was property protected by Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights art. 10 and by the takings clause of the Fourteenth Amendment of the federal constitution. Because there was no specific provision providing for the repayment of the bondholders, the court ruled that the appropriation of the bondholders' property was inconsistent with their right to receive compensation under Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights amend. art. 48.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the attorney general's certification that an initiative petition did not conflict with the state constitution and ordered the county court to enter a judgment declaring that the certification did conflict with the state constitution.

 

24 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Eakin


SJC-07647


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


427 Mass. 590; 696 N.E.2d 499; 1998 Mass. LEXIS 317


April 10, 1998, Argued  
June 4, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Middlesex. Complaints received and sworn to in the Newton Division of the District Court Department on December 9, 1991. On appeal to the Cambridge Division, the cases were tried before Arthur Sherman, J. After review by the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court granted leave to obtain further appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a judgment from the Appeals Court (Massachusetts), which reversed the judgment of the trial court convicting defendants of violations of the State Building Code with respect to a house they owned.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court reversed the convictions because, in its view, the building inspector had not given defendants adequate notice under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 143, § 51, for many of the alleged code violations, setting forth what changes were necessary to meet the requirements of the State Building Code. On appeal, the court found that although it seemed illogical that the owner of a private home was entitled to less advance notice of steps that should be taken to correct a building code violation than was the owner of a commercial or industrial building covered by § 51, such a determination was a legislative judgment. The court held that the state, inappropriately but without objection, had been required at the jury trial to prove compliance with § 51's notice requirement. The court concluded that its decision that § 51 was inapplicable to single-family residences would not unconstitutionally apply a retroactive redefinition of the crime with which defendants were charged. The court reversed the convictions and remanded for a retrial because since the charges were unsupported by a detailed notice of required remedial action, various charges could have been impermissibly vague.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment convicting defendants of violations of the State Building Code, set aside the verdicts, and remanded for a new trial.

 

25 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


New York Times Co. v. Commissioner of Revenue


SJC-07599, SJC-07654


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


427 Mass. 399; 693 N.E.2d 682; 1998 Mass. LEXIS 185


March 2, 1998, Argued  
May 7, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Appeal from a decision of the Appellate Tax Board. The Supreme Judicial Court granted an application for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review of the decision of the Massachusetts Appellate Tax Board, which upheld appellee commissioner of revenue's separate imposition of excise tax on each taxpayers' use of their aircraft in the commonwealth.


OVERVIEW: The department of revenue gave notice of its intention to separately impose use taxes on two taxpayers, pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 641, § 2, for their use of aircraft in the commonwealth. The taxpayers each unsuccessfully challenged the notice of intention to assess, and paid the use taxes. The taxpayers each made applications for abatement of taxes, which appellee commissioner of revenue (commissioner) separately denied. The Appellate Tax Board (board) upheld the commissioner's decisions. On appeal, the court affirmed the board's decisions. The court concluded that the commissioner did not have any clear policy exempting the use of aircraft from the Massachusetts use tax. The court held that the taxpayers could not insist that assessment of use taxes for their use of aircraft was exceptional, and violative of the equal protection guarantees of the Fourteenth Amendment and Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights art. 10, and the taxpayers had failed to adduce any evidence showing that other aircraft relevantly similar to their own aircraft existed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate tax board's decisions upholding the commissioner of revenue's imposition of excise taxes on the taxpayers for their use of aircraft in the Commonwealth.

 

26 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Lily Transp. Corp. v. Board of Assessors


SJC-07562


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


427 Mass. 228; 692 N.E.2d 53; 1998 Mass. LEXIS 165


February 5, 1998, Argued  
April 10, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Appeal from a decision of the Appellate Tax Board. The Supreme Judicial Court granted an application for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation challenged the decision of the Appellate Tax Board (Massachusetts), which affirmed the denial by the city board of assessors of the corporation's application for abatement of a motor vehicle excise imposed on a truck.


OVERVIEW: The corporation purchased a truck for $ 53,660. The city used the truck's list price of $ 84,332 rather than its sale price in calculating the excise tax. The Board upheld the assessment. On appeal, the corporation claimed that the application of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 60A, § 1 was unconstitutional. The court affirmed the determination, holding that the value of each motor vehicle was deemed to be the value of motor vehicles of the same make, type, model, and year of manufacture as designated by the manufacturer, but not in excess of stated percentages. The use of a truck's list price to calculate an excise was not an irrebutable presumption that violated due process, nor was using a rough approximation to calculate the excise wholly arbitrary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the corporation's application for abatement of a motor vehicle excise imposed on a truck.

 

27 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Duracraft Corp. v. Holmes Prods. Corp.


SJC-07519


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


427 Mass. 156; 691 N.E.2d 935; 1998 Mass. LEXIS 158; 13 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1479


December 8, 1997, Argued  
March 25, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on March 21, 1996. Special motions to dismiss were heard by Margaret R. Hinkle, J. After review by the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court granted leave to obtain further appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a competitor and former employee, sought review of the interlocutory order by the Appeals Court (Massachusetts), which denied their special motions, under G.L. c. 231, § 59H, to dismiss plaintiff former employer's claim that defendant former employee breached a confidentiality agreement.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff former employer brought an action against defendants, a competitor and former employee, after defendant employee began working for defendant competitor and during adjudicatory trademark proceedings between the parties. Defendant former employee testified to questions elicited by defendant competitor that plaintiff claimed breached confidentiality. Defendants then filed special motions to dismiss plaintiff's complaint, pursuant to G. L. c. 231, § 59H, the anti-Strategic Lawsuits Against Public Participation statute. After the motions were denied by the courts below, the court granted review. The court concluded that to avail themselves of § 59H, defendants had to make a threshold showing through the pleadings and affidavits that the claims against them were based on the petitioning activities alone and had no substantial basis other than or in addition to the petitioning activities. Because plaintiff had submitted a copy of the nondisclosure agreement to the court, which constituted a substantial basis other than defendants' petitioning activity to support plaintiff's claims, defendants' special motions failed. The judgment below was affirmed and the case remanded.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the court below denying special motions by defendants, a competitor and former employee, to dismiss plaintiff former employer's complaint against them and remanded the case for further proceedings because plaintiff had a substantial basis outside of its pleadings upon which to supports its claims of defendants' breach of confidentiality.

 

28 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Shaari v. Harvard Student Agencies


SJC-07479


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


427 Mass. 129; 691 N.E.2d 925; 1998 Mass. LEXIS 154; 26 Media L. Rep. 1730


January 8, 1998, Argued  
March 20, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Middlesex. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on November 15, 1990. The case was heard by Catherine A. White, J., on a motion for summary judgment, and a question of law was reported by Margot Botsford, J., to the Appeals Court. The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct review.



DISPOSITION: Order denying summary judgment reversed and entry of summary judgment for the defendants ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff manager filed a libel action against defendants, an author and a publisher, alleging that they made defamatory statements about the manager in their travel guide. The trial court denied the author and publisher's motion for summary judgment, primarily relying on Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 231, § 92. A question of law was reported to the Appeals Court (Massachusetts), and the court granted a request for direct review.


OVERVIEW: An edition of the author and publisher's travel guide stated, in reference to the manager's youth hostel, that women should not stay there, nor should men who did not want to encourage harassment. Three women were suing the manager on sexual harassment charges. Another edition of the guide recommended that travelers not stay there unless the management changed. The two statements were the basis of the libel action. The claim as to the first statement was time barred. The author and publisher claimed that the truthfulness of their statement regarding the sexual harassment allegations precluded any valid libel claim. The court concluded that § 92 unconstitutionally infringed on the author and publisher's freedom of speech, as guaranteed by U.S. Const. amend. I and Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights art., as amended by 16 Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights amend. art. 77. The court concluded, as a matter of state constitutional law, that the author and publisher were members of the "media." Therefore, the manager had to show that the defamatory statements were untrue in order to recover on his claim.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and ordered the entry of judgment for the author and publisher.

 

29 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Brown


SJC-07449


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


426 Mass. 475; 688 N.E.2d 1356; 1998 Mass. LEXIS 20


November 6, 1997, Argued  
January 15, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Complaint received and sworn to in the Boston Municipal Court Department on October 4, 1995. After the defendant admitted to sufficient facts to warrant findings of guilty before Patricia E. Bernstein, J., a motion for forfeiture was heard by her. The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of forfeiture vacated and case remanded to Boston Municipal Court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Boston Municipal Court Department (Massachusetts), which ordered a forfeiture of $ 142 as money attributable to the sale of controlled substances as provided in Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 94C, § 47(a)(5).


OVERVIEW: The defendant was charged with unlawful distribution of crack cocaine, and immediately following the disposition of the criminal case, the trial court considered the commonwealth's forfeiture motion for $ 142 seized at the time of the defendant's arrest. The trial court granted the motion, and the defendant sought review. On appeal, the defendant claimed that the commonwealth failed to meet its burden of showing probable cause to institute forfeiture proceedings and that the allocation to him of the burden of proof in Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 94C, § 47 violated the due process clause of the Fourteenth Amendment. The court found that § 47 did not violate the defendant's due process rights, and that the commonwealth did demonstrate probable cause, but that it failed to give the defendant adequate notice of the forfeiture.


OUTCOME: The court vacated and remanded the trial court's order granting the commonwealth's motion for forfeiture.

 

30 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


National Private Truck Council v. Commissioner


SJC-07478


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


426 Mass. 324; 688 N.E.2d 936; 1997 Mass. LEXIS 417


September 5, 1997, Argued  
December 22, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied May 26, 1998, Reported at: 1998 U.S. LEXIS 3450.


PRIOR HISTORY: Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on September 30, 1993. The case was heard by David M. Roseman, J., on a statement of agreed facts. The Supreme Judicial Court granted an application for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Declaration entered by Superior Court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant revenue commissioner (commissioner) appealed the judgment from the Superior Court of Suffolk County (Massachusetts), which declared that Mass. Regs. Code tit. 830, § 63.39.1(5) (1993), regarding the state's excise tax, as applied to the members of plaintiff trade association, was preempted by 15 U.S.C.S. § 381 and that § 381 was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The trade association had more than 1,000 foreign corporation members that operated their own truck fleets to deliver their products. The members solicited sales of tangible goods in the state. The orders were sent outside the state for approval and were filled outside the state. Based on the members' use of their own trucks to make deliveries in the state, the commissioner imposed excise taxes against them under Mass. Regs. Code tit. 830, § 63.39.1(5) (1993) (regulation). The trade association sought a declaration that 15 U.S.C.S. § 381 preempted the regulation. The superior court entered judgment for the trade association. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. Section 381 precluded state income taxes on foreign corporations whose business within the state consisted solely of the solicitation for sales of tangible goods, which orders were sent outside the state for approval and were filled outside the state. The statute did not require that the transfer occur outside the state. Congress had the authority under the commerce clause to prohibit states from imposing taxes that interfered with interstate commerce. Thus, the Tenth Amendment was not implicated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's judgment declaring that federal law preempted the state regulation regarding excise taxes and that the federal law was constitutional.

 

31 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Doe v. AG


SJC-07481


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


426 Mass. 136; 686 N.E.2d 1007; 1997 Mass. LEXIS 395


September 5, 1997, Argued  
November 17, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on September 30, 1996. The case was reported to the Appeals Court by Patrick J. King, J., on a statement of agreed facts. The Supreme Judicial Court granted an application for direct review.



DISPOSITION: A judgment shall be entered in the Superior Court declaring that the registration requirements and notification provisions of G. L. c. 6, §§ 178I-178O, are unconstitutional as applied to the plaintiff in the absence of a right to a hearing and, if a hearing is requested, to a determination concerning his threat, if any, to minors and others for whose protection the act was passed. An injunction shall be issued in the Superior Court enjoining the defendants from requiring the plaintiff to register under the sex offender act and from distributing or releasing any information concerning the plaintiff pursuant to that act, in the absence of a determination following a hearing concerning the plaintiff's threat, if any, to others.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff was convicted of indecent assault and battery prior to the passage of the sex offender act (act), Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 6, §§ 178C-178O. Under the act, plaintiff was a level one sex offender and would be required to comply with registration and notification requirements. Plaintiff challenged the constitutionality of the act by an action filed in Superior Court (Massachusetts), and reported to the court on a statement of agreed facts.


OVERVIEW: The court granted direct review to plaintiff's complaint challenging the constitutionality of the registration and notification requirements of the sex offender act (act), Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 6, §§ 178C-178O, as they applied to plaintiff, who was convicted of indecent assault and battery. Plaintiff contended that the act's automatic classification of him as a level one sex offender deprived him of procedural due process in violation of the state and federal constitutions. The court held that the act unconstitutionally denied plaintiff procedural due process rights guaranteed by the state constitution. The court ordered that an injunction should be issued enjoining the state from requiring plaintiff to register under the sex offender act and from distributing or releasing any information concerning plaintiff pursuant to that act, in the absence of a determination following a hearing concerning plaintiff's threat, if any, to minors and others for whose protection the act was passed.


OUTCOME: The court directed the trial court to enter a judgment declaring that the registration requirements and notification provisions of the sex offender act are unconstitutional as applied to plaintiff in the absence of a right to a hearing and, if a hearing is requested, to a determination concerning his threat, if any, to minors and others for whose protection the act was passed. The court also ordered injunctive relief for plaintiff.

 

32 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Answer of the Justices to the Acting Governor


SJC-07544


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


686 N.E.2d 444; 1997 Mass. LEXIS 382



October 30, 1997, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [**1] Justices respectfully decline to answer the Acting Governor's questions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Propounder, the acting governor of the Commonwealth of Massachusetts (governor), submitted questions related to petitions regarding term limits, when the governor could call a joint session of the legislature if it did not take action on the petitions, and whether the governor could require the legislature to take action on a proposed constitutional amendment pending before that body.


OVERVIEW: The court found that Mass. Const. art. 2, cl. 3 when strictly construed prevented the court from responding to the governor's questions. Regarding the petitions pending before the legislature and whether they were substantially similar to an existing statute, the court held that under Mass. Const. art. 48, The Initiative, Part II, § 3, the attorney general had to make that determination. Therefore, the court was not asked to answer a question related to the governor's power or authority, and because no solemn occasion existed the court could not respond. On the next question, the governor's concern over the possibility that the legislature might have refused to act on petitions before it, again did not raise a solemn occasion. Thus, the court declined to answer. The governor's final questions regarding when he could call a joint session or require the legislature to take action on matters if it chose not to, the court held that these questions sought advisory opinions because they were not based upon any existing occasion that called for an opinion. Therefore, the court again declined to answer.


OUTCOME: The court declined to give advisory opinions to each of the governor's questions.

Town of Plymouth v. Civil Serv. Comm'n


SJC-07405


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


426 Mass. 1; 686 N.E.2d 188; 1997 Mass. LEXIS 372; 13 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 650


September 8, 1997, Argued  
October 20, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Plymouth. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on September 7, 1994. The entry of a judgment of dismissal was ordered by John J. O'Brien, J. The Supreme Judicial Court granted an application for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Judgment vacated. New judgment to enter setting aside commission's decision ordering Rossborough's conditional reinstatement and upholding town's decision to terminate her.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff town sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts), which dismissed the town's action against defendant Civil Service Commission (commission) that was brought after the commission ordered a terminated police officer restored to the officer's position upon demonstration that the officer no longer used tobacco products in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 41, § 101A.


OVERVIEW: After the police officer was caught smoking on duty, the town terminated the officer pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 41, § 101A's smoking prohibition and the personnel administration rules implementing § 101A. Based on its practice of allowing flexibility in the treatment of employees who habitually used alcohol in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 31, § 50, the commission determined that Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 41, § 101A had not required mandatory termination and ordered the officer reinstated upon demonstration that the officer no longer used tobacco. Thereafter, the town brought an action against the commission. When the trial court dismissed the action, the town sought review. In vacating the judgment and upholding the town's decision to terminate the officer, the court held the personnel administration rules, which had required mandatory termination, had been consistent with the legislative directive. Thus, the rules had acquired the force of law. Moreover, the court noted that while Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 31, § 50 contained discretionary language, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 41, § 101A contained no such language, and that the legislative purposes behind the two statutes was different.


OUTCOME: The court vacated a judgment dismissing the town's action against the commission that was brought after the commission ordered a terminated police officer restored to the officer's position upon demonstration that the officer no longer used tobacco products. Moreover, the court entered a judgment setting aside the commission's decision ordering the officer's conditional reinstatement and upholding the town's decision to terminate the officer.
