Liability Investigative Fund Effort v. Massachusetts Medical Professional Ins. Ass'n


Hd-6454


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


418 Mass. 436; 636 N.E.2d 1317; 1994 Mass. LEXIS 459


April 7, 1994, Argued  
July 21, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended August 29, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Hampden. Civil actions commenced in the Superior Court Department on June 2, 1988, and May 3, 1989, respectively. The cases were heard by Richard F. Connon, J., on motions for summary judgment. The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporation sought review of the judgment from the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts) that granted summary judgment in favor of defendant association in the corporation's action seeking to declare two statutes relating to the provision of medical malpractice insurance to be unconstitutional. Both parties filed motions for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The association was authorized to issue malpractice insurance policies to physicians and hospitals that had made a reasonable effort to obtain insurance and were unable to obtain it. Both the deficit recoupment statute, 1975 Mass. Acts ch. 362, § 6, as amended by 1980 Mass. Acts ch. 333, and the deferred premium liability statute, 1986 Mass. Acts ch. 351, provided for payments by malpractice insureds for costs incurred by the association in providing malpractice insurance in past years. The corporation challenged the statutes on the basis that they violated the contracts clause, state and federal guarantees of procedural due process, and the separation of powers provisions of the Declaration of Rights. In affirming, the court held that neither the deficit recoupment statute, nor the deferred premium liability statute violated the contracts clause of the United States Constitution, state or federal guarantees of procedural due process, or the separation of powers requirements of Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights art. 30.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment from the lower court granting the association summary judgment in the corporation's action seeking to declare two statutes unconstitutional under the contracts clause of the United States Constitution.

 

103 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Provost


W-6545


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


418 Mass. 416; 636 N.E.2d 1312; 1994 Mass. LEXIS 457


May 3, 1994, Argued  
July 20, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Worcester. Indictment found and returned in the Superior Department on September 17, 1992. The case was heard by Daniel F. Toomey, J. The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On the motion of the court, the case was transferred from the Appeals Court (Massachusetts). At the end of the jury-waived trial, the trial court denied defendant's motion to dismiss the indictment and denied the motion for a required finding of not guilty. The trial court found defendant guilty of the taking of photographs of a partially nude child with lascivious intent, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, § 29A (1992), and sentenced him.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted on one count of violating Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, § 29A (1992). The trial court denied defendant's motion to dismiss the indictment. At the close of his jury-waived trial, the trial court denied defendant's motion for a required finding of not guilty, and he was found guilty and sentenced to a 10 year suspended prison term and 5 years probation with certain restrictions on his activities. Defendant argued that his conduct did not violate § 29A(a), and that §§ 29A(a), 31 (1992), were constitutionally infirm in that they criminalized the depiction of nudity per se and because they criminalized intent without attendant conduct. The court transferred the case on its own motion and affirmed defendant's conviction. The court found that the taking of photographs of a partially nude child with lascivious intent was conduct that § 29A was designed to prevent. The court further found that the commonwealth's compelling interest in protecting and safeguarding the physical and psychological well being of the child, therefore, allowed the application of §§ 29A, 31 to defendant's conduct. The court found that the statute avoided any overbreadth problems.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's conviction of defendant for the taking of photographs of a partially nude child with lascivious intent.

 

104 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Attorney Gen. v. Desilets


F-6284


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


418 Mass. 316; 636 N.E.2d 233; 1994 Mass. LEXIS 396


February 8, 1994, Argued  
July 14, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Franklin. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on October 4, 1990. The case was heard by George C. Keady, Jr., J., on motions for summary judgment. The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff attorney general sought review, by application for direct appellate review, the decision of the Superior Court of Franklin County (Massachusetts), which granted, on cross-motions for summary judgment, defendant landlords' motion for summary judgment, and denied the attorney general's in his case for the landlords' violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 151B, § 4(6) when the landlord denied rental occupancy to an unmarried couple.


OVERVIEW: Defendant landlords owned apartment buildings. The landlords declined to consider leasing an apartment to an unmarried couple because they had a policy of not leasing to any person who intended to engage in conduct that violated their religious principles. As Roman Catholics, the landlords believed that they should not facilitate sinful conduct, including fornication. The attorney general commenced the action on behalf of the unmarried couple. The lower court ruled that the landlords had violated § 4(6), but that application of the statute to the landlords was unconstitutional. The court found that the case involved the tension between a statutory mandate that a landlord must not discriminate against unmarried couples in renting accommodations and the landlords' sincerely held religious beliefs that they should not facilitate what they regard as sinful cohabitation. The court held that the landlords violated § 4(6), but vacated the judgment and remanded the case because the Commonwealth was to be given the opportunity to demonstrate a compelling interest in the application of the statute, in view of its denying the landlords a statutory exemption.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment for the landlords and remanded the case to the lower court for further consideration. The court concluded that neither party was entitled to summary judgment.

 

105 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Irish-American Gay, Lesbian & Bisexual Group v. City of Boston


S-6498


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


418 Mass. 238; 636 N.E.2d 1293; 1994 Mass. LEXIS 388


March 10, 1994, Argued  
July 11, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on March 10, 1992. The case was heard by J. Harold Flannery, J. The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant parade organizers sought review of a decision of the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts), which granted permanent injunctive relief to the plaintiffs, gay organization and members (collectively, the organization), to enjoin the parade organizers from discriminating against the organization on the basis of sexual orientation in violation of the public accommodation discrimination law, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, §§ 92A, 98.


OVERVIEW: The parade organizers refused to allow the organization to participate in its annual parade because of the organizers' decision to exclude groups with sexual themes. The trial court found that the exclusion of the organization was a form of sexual orientation discrimination in violation of the public accommodation discrimination law and further found that inconsistent explanations for excluding the organization and the lack of selection standards were pretextual. The court held: 1) the trial court's determination was not clearly erroneous because the plain language of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272 § 92A(8) established that the parade fell within the scope of the public accommodation law; 2) the parade organizers failed to established that the parade was for expressive purposes for First Amendment protection; and 3) the public accommodation law facially did not reach speech or expression protected by the First Amendment, it did not infringe on the parade organizers' rights, and it gave persons of ordinary intelligence a reasonable opportunity to know what was prohibited by the law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court in favor of the organization.

 

106 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Salusti v. Town of Watertown


M-6482


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


418 Mass. 202; 635 N.E.2d 249; 1994 Mass. LEXIS 391


May 3, 1994, Argued  
July 7, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Middlesex. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on July 5, 1990. A motion to dismiss was heard by Margot Botsford, J.; a motion for summary judgment was heard by Catherine A. White, J.; and a motion to reconsider the prior motion for summary judgment was heard by Elizabeth Butler, J. The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff realty trustees brought two claims against defendant, the town of Watertown, under the Massachusetts Tort Claims Act, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 258, § 2 (1992). The superior court (Massachusetts) dismissed count one, which alleged negligent inspection of and failure to repair fire hydrants, and granted summary judgment on count two, which alleged negligent firefighting. The trustees appealed.


OVERVIEW: A commercial office building owned by the trust and located in the town caught fire. The town's fire department reported to the scene and attempted to contain and extinguish the fire. The complaint alleged that the fire department was unable to contain the fire successfully because of an inadequate water supply and because of negligent firefighting tactics. The trustees argued that the public duty rule did not preclude their claims. The court affirmed the judgment for the town because the duty to provide an adequate supply of water for fighting fires, consistent with the general duty to provide fire protection, was a duty owed to the public at large, and the town's liability was precluded by the public duty rule. That a hydrant in a state of disrepair was in the vicinity of the trustees property was not sufficient to create a special duty. Common law precluded actions against municipalities for negligent firefighting.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the claim for negligent inspection of and failure to repair fire hydrants and summary judgment on the claim of negligent firefighting.

 

107 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Murphy v. Commissioner of the Dep't of Indus. Accidents


S-6417


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


418 Mass. 165; 635 N.E.2d 1180; 1994 Mass. LEXIS 385


March 7, 1994, Argued  
July 6, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on July 23, 1992. Following the decision of this court in 415 Mass. 218 (1993), a motion for expedited entry of judgment was heard by Margaret R. Hinkle, J. The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff individual sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts), which held that a portion of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 152, § 11A (1991) was unconstitutional because it required that a claimant represented by counsel submit a fee not required by other claimants.


OVERVIEW: The court held that a portion of § 11A was unconstitutional because it required that a claimant represented by counsel submit a fee not required by other claimants. The court held that this classification violated the equal protection provisions of the constitution of the commonwealth, in that it was not supported by any rational basis. On appeal, the court affirmed its judgment, holding that the provision was unconstitutional because it arbitrarily and without rational basis classified claimants based on whether they were proceeding with the assistance of an attorney. The court held that the amount of the fee bore no clear relation to the stated purpose of the fee but did not rule that the words were unconstitutional as a violation of equal protection or due process. The court subsequently granted defendant commissioner's emergency motion, which sought to enter a declaration that the phrases "represented by counsel" and "equal to the average weekly wage in the commonwealth at the time of the appeal" were unconstitutional. The court held that the remainder of the section, including the words retained in the sentence regarding the fee, remained valid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, holding that the fee provision violated the equal protection clause.

 

108 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


City of Boston v. Back Bay Cultural Ass'n


S-6490


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


418 Mass. 175; 635 N.E.2d 1175; 1994 Mass. LEXIS 384


April 5, 1994, Argued  
July 6, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on January 26, 1993. The case was heard by Richard S. Kelley, J., on motions for summary judgment. The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a local club and related individuals, appealed an order of the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts), which held on cross motions for summary judgment that Boston, Mass., Code § 17-13.6 (1985), a noise ordinance enacted by plaintiff, the city of Boston, did not violate either Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 140, § 183A (1992), the state licensing law, or the First Amendment.


OVERVIEW: Under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 140, § 183A (1992), no person was allowed to operate a club and to provide public entertainment without a license. Boston, Mass., Code § 17-13.6 (1985), a noise ordinance, provided that businesses that held entertainment licenses could not operate between 2:00 a.m. and 6:00 a.m., with the exception of films that began before 12:30 p.m. and closed before 3:00 a.m. The city granted a local club a license on condition that it complied with the ordinance. On cross motions for summary judgment by the city and the club, the superior court upheld the ordinance as valid under both the state statute and the First Amendment. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision as to the state statute but reversed on the First Amendment analysis. The noise ordinance fulfilled a legitimate governmental purpose and was content neutral. However, the ordinance failed constitutional muster because its time, place, and manner restrictions were not narrowly tailored to fit its purpose. The city admitted that the ordinance adversely affected entertainment that did not produce the unwanted secondary effects of noise.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's ruling that the city's noise ordinance did not violate state law; however, the court reversed the ruling that the ordinance did not violate the First Amendment. The court held that although the ordinance was content neutral and its purpose acceptable, it was not narrowly tailored.

 

109 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Smith


Hd-6439


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


418 Mass. 120; 634 N.E.2d 1380; 1994 Mass. LEXIS 315


April 6, 1994, Argued  
June 14, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected July 12, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Hampden. Indictment found and returned in the Superior Court Department on January 13, 1989. The case was tried before Elizabeth A. Porada, J. The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction in the trial court (Massachusetts) for trafficking in cocaine, a violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 94C, § 32E(b)(4) (1992).


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction, claiming that the trial court's failure to allow his motion to sever his trial from that of a co-defendant resulted in a denial of defendant's federal and state constitutional rights to present a full defense. The court determined that defendant supported his co-defendant's claim that the police fabricated his arrest by planting drugs and that defendant portrayed himself as an innocent victim who was arrested because he witnessed alleged police misconduct, the court ruled that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying the motion to sever because the defenses presented by both defendants were united and common. Noting that defendant's argument was in reality grounded on the trial court's limitation of his cross-examination of witnesses as to the duration of the police department's investigation of his co-defendant rather than on a failure to sever, the court ruled that the record did not support defendant's contention that exclusion of this evidence prevented him from arguing that he had been framed to preserve the case against the co-defendant, and that defendant was not deprived of exculpatory evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for trafficking in cocaine.

Latimore v. Commonwealth


S-6409


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


417 Mass. 805; 633 N.E.2d 396; 1994 Mass. LEXIS 297


April 4, 1994, Argued  
May 16, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on October 28, 1992. The case was heard by Wilkins, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk (Massachusetts) that denied his request for attorney fees and costs in a case in which he was convicted of first-degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder in the first degree. Defendant's motion for a new trial was granted by the superior court. The issue before the court was whether defendant could be awarded attorney's fees and costs of appeal after the commonwealth's application for leave to appeal was denied. The single justice of the superior court reasoned that a request to a single justice for leave to appeal did not constitute an appeal to an appellate court from a final order as required by Mass. R. Crim. P. 30(c)(8)(B). The single justice denied defendant's request for attorney's fees and costs. The court affirmed, holding that defendant had no basis for recovery of attorney's fees and costs. The court concluded that an award of attorney's fees and costs was not appropriate because there was no statute or rule providing for the payment of attorneys fees and costs to a defendant when a single justice denied the commonwealth's application for leave to appeal under Mass. Gen. Laws. ch. 278, § 33E.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the superior court that denied defendant's request for attorney's fees and costs.

Redgate


S-6503


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


417 Mass. 799; 633 N.E.2d 380; 1994 Mass. LEXIS 242


April 7, 1994, Argued  
May 12, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Petition filed in the Superior Court Department on November 15, 1989. The case was heard by Richard F. Stearns, J. After review by the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court granted leave to obtain further appellate review.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate requested that the court hold unconstitutional his commitment to a treatment center as a sexually dangerous person (SDP) under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 123A, § 6, as appearing in 1985 Mass. Acts 752, § 1. The appeals court (Massachusetts) held that the commitment ordered by the trial court was unconstitutional. The court granted the commonwealth's application for further appellate review.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was serving sentences for crimes committed prior to April 6, 1986, and therefore, under 1985 Mass. Acts 752, § 4, was subject to the less stringent, preamendment version of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 123A, § 6 and his commitment proceedings were instituted without him having committed any sexually assaultive behavior while under sentence. The trial court committed the inmate to a treatment center and denied his later petition for discharge. The appellate court held the inmate's commitment unconstitutional and, on appeal, the court affirmed. The court considered the inmate's challenge to his commitment because its constitutional significance was not established until after the proceedings conducted under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 123A, §§ 6, 9, when the court entered judgment in a similar case. The court held that the inmate's right to equal protection of the laws was violated. Because the court held that the inmate's initial commitment to the treatment center was constitutionally infirm, and it vacated the denial of the petition under § 9, it did not address whether the trial judge's order was supported by sufficient evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the appellate court, vacated the trial court's denial of the inmate's petition for discharge from the treatment center, and vacated the initial order of the commitment of the inmate as an SDP.

Commonwealth v. Perito


P-6372


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


417 Mass. 674; 632 N.E.2d 1190; 1994 Mass. LEXIS 229


January 5, 1994, Argued  
May 5, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Plymouth. Complaint received and sworn to in the Wareham Division of the District Court Department on February 21, 1989. A bail hearing was held by Roger B. Champagne, J. Indictments found and returned in the Superior Court Department, two on May 1, 1989, one on February 16, 1990, and one on June 5, 1990, respectively. A pretrial motion to suppress evidence was heard by William H. Carey, J.; pretrial motions to dismiss and for production of complete files were heard by Suzanne DelVecchio, J.; and the cases were tried before Cortland A. Mathers, J. The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from four armed robbery convictions entered in the trial court (Massachusetts), grounding his complaint in an allegedly illegal detention. The case was transferred on the court's own initiative to consider whether a district court judge could set bail in a defendant's absence and order him committed to a house of correction pending a postponed arraignment when medical necessity precluded his immediate appearance in court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for receiving a stolen motor vehicle, driving to endanger, and failing to stop for the police. Because defendant posed a danger to himself, the district court judge issued a mittimus ordering that he be committed to a house of correction pending appearance at his pretrial hearing that was postponed due to a staff psychologist's opinion that he was suicidal, and that he should be committed to the state hospital for a period of observation not to exceed 30 days. Defendant was arraigned following his release from the state hospital on charges for various armed robberies to which the police had connected him using the photographs and fingerprints taken at the house of correction.The court agreed that the district court judge's practice violated defendant's right to participate in his bail hearing and his right to a prompt initial court appearance. Consequently, defendant was illegally detained. There was no basis for dismissing the indictments or suppressing evidence as a remedy, as defendant failed to demonstrate prejudice to his case caused by the violation of his rights, and failed to show that there had been egregious misconduct by the Commonwealth.


OUTCOME: The judgment and convictions were affirmed.

Town of Brookline v. Secretary


S-6485


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


417 Mass. 406; 631 N.E.2d 968; 1994 Mass. LEXIS 155


March 8, 1994, Argued  
March 31, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Civil actions commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on December 14, 1993, and in the Supreme Judicial Court for the Commonwealth on December 15, 1993, respectively. The Suffolk County action was transferred by Abrams, J., to the Supreme Judicial Court for the Commonwealth and the cases were consolidated for hearing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff towns filed suit in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk (Massachusetts) and in the Supreme Judicial Court for mandamus against defendant commonwealth secretary to invalidate the redistricting plan for the 160 House of Representatives districts. The towns asserted that Mass. Gen. Law, ch. 273, § 1 was unconstitutional under Amendments to Mass. Const., art. 101 and Mass. Declaration of Rights, arts. 1, 7, 8, 9.


OVERVIEW: The commonwealth legislature enacted Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 273, § 1, which established 160 districts for the House of Representatives. The redistricting plan was required under Amendments to Mass. Const., art. 101. Art. 101 specified that any challenge to the plan was to be filed within 10 days in the Supreme Judicial Court. The towns filed suit in the lower court, then filed again the next day in the proper court. The court held that the delay did not necessitate dismissing the suit, but it denied the request on the merits. The court held that the redistricting plan met the commonwealth's constitutional requirements and properly included the goals established under the Federal Voting Rights. It held that the towns had not presented a better plan that would effectuate the one person, one vote rule and the reapportionment requirements of the commonwealth's constitution. It held that its role was not to create a better redistricting plan, but to evaluate whether the plan as drafted met the federal and commonwealth constitutional requirements. It held that the legislature had created a plan that complied with those requirements.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the action filed in the lower court. The court held that the redistricting plan for the 160 districts for the House of Representatives was not unconstitutional and denied the request for mandamus filed by the towns.

Lopes v. City of Peabody


S-6368


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


417 Mass. 299; 629 N.E.2d 1312; 1994 Mass. LEXIS 101


December 8, 1993, Argued  
March 14, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended March 24, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Land Court Department on December 12, 1989. The case was heard by Marilyn M. Sullivan, J. After review by the Appeals Court and remand to that court by the Supreme Court of the United States, the Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct review.
Lopes v. City of Peabody, 507 U.S. 981, 113 S. Ct. 1574, 123 L. Ed. 2d 142, 1993 U.S. LEXIS 2150 (1993)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff owner challenged the decision of the Appeals Court (Massachusetts), which affirmed the trial court's ruling that defendant city's determination of 88.5 feet as the minimum permitted elevation in the wetlands conservancy district was a valid exercise of legislative discretion, was not arbitrary or unreasonable, was enforceable as applied to plaintiff's lot, and was not a taking.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff owner brought an action against defendant city challenging the validity of a section of a zoning ordinance because the elevation of all but a small portion of his lot was below the 88.5-foot contour of the wetlands conservancy district. The trial court held that the determination of 88.5 feet as the minimum permitted elevation in the wetlands conservancy district was a valid exercise of legislative discretion, was not arbitrary or unreasonable, was enforceable as applied to plaintiff's lot, and was not a taking. The appellate court affirmed, plaintiff appealed, and the case was remanded. The court held that the ordinance's validity could be challenged by plaintiff as a purchaser of the land subject to the restriction. The court remanded to the trial court for an evaluation of the applicable standards for determining whether there had been a regulatory taking of property. The court concluded that a finding had to be made as to whether application of the ordinance had caused plaintiff's land to have no economically beneficial use and whether plaintiff could prove that the zoning restriction did not substantially advance legitimate state interests as applied to his lot.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's judgment affirming the trial court's ruling that the determination of 88.5 feet as the minimum permitted elevation in the wetlands conservancy district was a valid exercise of legislative discretion and remanded to the trial court for a determination under the applicable standards for determining whether there had been a regulatory taking of property.

 

115 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commissioner v. Chinchillo


S-6380


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


417 Mass. 219; 629 N.E.2d 974; 1994 Mass. LEXIS 91


December 7, 1993, Argued  
March 8, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Appeal from a decision of the Appellate Tax Board. The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Decision of the Appellate Tax Board reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Commissioner of Revenue sought review from the Appellate Tax Board (Massachusetts), which determined that appellee nonresident taxpayers were not required to pay Massachusetts income taxes on the interest they received on a purchase money mortgage note because they had paid the state tax due on the sale in the year of the sale. The Commissioner of Revenue asserted that such future interest income was not exempt from taxation.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers sold real estate they owned in Massachusetts, structuring the sale as an "installment sale" of property under 26 U.S.C.S. § 453(b) for federal income tax purposes while electing, for Massachusetts tax purposes, to report and pay the entire tax on the gain in their 1982 nonresident income tax returns, as provided by Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 62, § 63(e) (1992). The commissioner contended that the interest income was not exempt from taxation for 1983-1986, and the court, in reversing the board, agreed. In so holding, the court reasoned that it was illogical to interpret the ambiguous language in § 63(e) as reaching out to exempt interest income from taxation for the years in question because the taxpayers had elected to pay state tax on the entire gain on the transaction in the year of the sale. Further, the court rejected the nonresident taxpayers' argument that such taxation was unconstitutional, finding that because the taxpayers had a mortgage on Massachusetts real estate to secure the debt owed to them by the purchasers, the benefit and protection that the law of Massachusetts extended to them provided sufficient basis for imposing the tax.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the Appellate Tax Board and held that the taxpayers were required to pay income tax for 1983-1986 on the interest income they received on the purchase money mortgage note they received from the buyers of their property.

Franklin Found. v. Attorney Gen.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


416 Mass. 483; 623 N.E.2d 1109; 1993 Mass. LEXIS 728


November 2, 1993, Argued  
December 6, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court+ for the county of Suffolk on June 20, 1990. The case was reported by Greaney, J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The plaintiff foundation sought review from an order of the Supreme Judicial Court for the County of Suffolk (Massachusetts), which declined to exercise power to terminate a trust under 1958 Mass. Acts ch. 596.


OVERVIEW: In a codicil to the decedent's will, he left money to the inhabitants of the city, provided the trust was used to grant loans to young married persons setting up business. The codicil further stated that if the plan was executed for 100 years, an amount would go to the city for use at their discretion for public works, and the remainder would continue in the grant program for the next 100 years, and then terminate. Subsequently, the legislature enacted 1958 Mass. Acts ch. 596, to pay the portion of the trust bequeathed to the city to a foundation, and the trust would not terminate unless a decree of the supreme judicial court authorized the termination. The foundation brought an interpleader action for termination of the trust under 1958 Mass. Acts ch. 596 because there were no loan recipients. The trial court declined to exercise its power to terminate the trust. On review, the court held that the trust term expired on the date of the second hundred years, and required immediate distribution of the corpus of the trust to the foundation. Neither distribution nor termination required court authorization based upon the termination language of the codicil.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case to the trial court for an entry of appropriate declaratory judgment confirming that the decedent's trust terminated on a date certain, and instructing that the distribution of the remainder of the trust funds be made in accordance with the codicil.

Jenkins v. Chief Justice of Dist. Court Dep't


S-6180


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


416 Mass. 221; 619 N.E.2d 324; 1993 Mass. LEXIS 529


May 4, 1993, Argued  
September 13, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on September 30, 1991. The case was reported by Wilkins, J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, two defendants arrested without warrants and the Committee for Public Counsel Services, petitioned the court pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 211, § 3, for an order that all warrantless arrests in the state be followed by a prompt judicial determination of probable cause on the completion of the administrative steps incident to arrest. Defendant justices opposed the petition and sought to dismiss the Committee as an improper party.


OVERVIEW: The court examined the history of the protections contained in the Fourth Amendment to the U.S. Constitution and art. 14 of the Massachusetts Declaration of Rights and concluded that the only element bearing on the reasonableness of the delay between a competed arrest and a judicial determination of probable cause was the time reasonably necessary to reach a magistrate. The court agreed with plaintiffs that, under normal circumstances, a 24-hour limit fairly reflected the required time, and noted that most federal cases agreed with that assessment. The court held that where that time limit was exceeded, the police must bear the burden of demonstrating that an extraordinary circumstance caused the delay. The court held that the probable cause determination must be made by a neutral and detached magistrate, could be made verbally in an ex parte proceeding as long as the art. 14 "oath" or "affirmation requirement was made, and that defendants were not entitled to assistance of counsel during the probable cause hearing. The case therefore remanded the case for the entry of a declaratory judgment reflecting its opinion.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case for entry of a declaratory judgment that persons who had been arrested without a warrant were entitled to a probable cause hearing in front of a neutral, detached magistrate within 24 hours of their arrest, barring extraordinary circumstances.

Commonwealth v. Twitchell


S-6115


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


416 Mass. 114; 617 N.E.2d 609; 1993 Mass. LEXIS 515


May 4, 1993, Argued  
August 11, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Indictments found and returned in the Superior Court Department on April 22, 1988. The cases were tried before Sandra L. Hamlin, J. The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed their convictions by the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts) for involuntary manslaughter on request of direct appeal.


OVERVIEW: In challenging their convictions, defendants claimed that the spiritual treatment provision of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 273, § 1 barred their prosecution because they were following the tenets of their Christian Science faith in refusing to get medical care for their son's peritonitis, which he died from. In conjunction with this argument, defendants alleged that given the provision and an opinion of the Massachusetts Attorney General on its effect, they did not receive fair warning that they could be charged with involuntary manslaughter. The court found that defendants were subject to a common law duty to provide for the care of their children, the breach of which could form the basis for an involuntary manslaughter charge. It found that the spiritual treatment provision did not foreclose an involuntary manslaughter charge and that the involuntary manslaughter statute gave fair warning to defendants. However, whether the Attorney General's opinion could have led defendants to believe that they did not need to obtain medical treatment for their son was a question of fact that should have been presented to the jury, and the failure to do so could have led to a miscarriage of justice.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendants' convictions for involuntary manslaughter.

Clean Harbors of Braintree, Inc. v. Board of Health


N-6141


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


415 Mass. 876; 616 N.E.2d 78; 1993 Mass. LEXIS 452


April 8, 1993, Argued  
July 19, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Norfolk. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on March 19, 1987. After review by this court, 409 Mass. 834 (1991), and entry of final judgment, a motion for relief from judgement was heard by Andrew G. Meyer, J. The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.
Clean Harbors of Braintree, Inc. v. Board of Health, 409 Mass. 834, 570 N.E.2d 987, 1991 Mass. LEXIS 197 (1991)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action by plaintiff corporation, defendant board of health (board) appealed an order of the Superior Court Department, Norfolk (Massachusetts), which granted the corporation's motion for relief from judgment and entered a new judgment in the corporation's favor, claiming that 23 Stat. 18 (1992), which amended Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 111, § 150B (1990), was unconstitutional and did not apply to the corporation.


OVERVIEW: The court originally held that Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 111, § 150B applied to the corporation and that to continue operations, it had to apply for and receive a site assignment from the board. The legislature then amended § 150B by providing, in 23 Stat. 18 (1992) (the amendment), that Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 111, §§ 150A, 150B did not apply to any hazardous waste facility which was so licensed as of May 1, 1980. The trial court granted the corporation's motion for relief from the judgment and a stay of further proceedings before the board. The board appealed, arguing that the amendment was unconstitutional. After granting the board's application for direct appellate review, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment, holding that the legislature properly amended the statute to accomplish what it originally intended. Further, the amendment was clearly enacted in response to the court's original judgment to exclude hazardous waste facilities such as that of the corporation. The court also ruled that the amendment did not violate the Home Rule Amendment of the state constitution because it concerned matters of state or general concern, even though it had a special effect on one town.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in favor of the corporation.

 

123 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


McDuffy v. Secretary of Executive Office of Educ.


S-6128


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


415 Mass. 545; 615 N.E.2d 516; 1993 Mass. LEXIS 372


February 2, 1993, Argued  
June 15, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on May 9, 1978. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on March 15, 1989. Proceedings under the first seven counts of the complaint in the second case were ordered transferred to the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk by Abrams, J., and the two cases were reported by her on a stipulation of agreed facts.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, 16 students in various public schools (students), filed actions against defendants, education officials (commonwealth), seeking a declaration of rights under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 231A (1990) that the commonwealth failed to fulfill its duty to provide them an education as mandated by Mass. Const. part II, c. 5, § 2.


OVERVIEW: Students filed actions against the commonwealth alleging that the commonwealth failed to fulfill its duty to provide them with an education as mandated by Mass. Const. part II, c. 5, § 2. After reviewing the history of the constitutional provision, the court declared that Part II, c. 5, § 2 imposed a mandatory, enforceable duty on the magistrates and legislatures of the commonwealth to provide education in the public schools for the children there enrolled, whether they be rich or poor and without regard to the fiscal capacity of the community or district in which such children lived. The court held that while local governments could be required, in part, to support public schools, it was the responsibility of the commonwealth to take such steps as was necessary to effectively devise a plan and sources of funds sufficient to meet the constitutional mandate. In this case, however, the court found that the commonwealth was not currently fulfilling its constitutional duty. Thus, the court set forth broad guidelines of education and left it to the commonwealth to take the necessary actions to remedy the failures in the current educational system and to fulfill its duty to educate.


OUTCOME: The court declared that the Massachusetts Constitution required the magistrates and legislatures of the commonwealth to provide education in the public schools for children, however, the court found that the commonwealth was not currently fulfilling this constitutional duty. Thus, the court ordered the commonwealth to remedy its failure and fulfill its duty to educate.

Delaney v. Commonwealth


S-5994


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


415 Mass. 490; 614 N.E.2d 672; 1993 Mass. LEXIS 367


February 4, 1993, Argued  
June 10, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on June 4, 1992. The case was heard by O'Connor, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought appellate review of the denial of his petition under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 211, § 3 (1990), by a single justice of the Supreme Judicial Court (Massachusetts) for relief from a bail revocation order.


OVERVIEW: When defendant's appeal was heard, the underlying criminal charges against him were dismissed and he was free. The court found that the appeal raised important issues that were likely to arise again, but were unlikely to be reviewed before becoming moot. The court therefore held that it was appropriate to reach the merits of the issues raised despite the absence of a live controversy. The full supreme court held that there was no requirement that the government institute any additional criminal proceeding as a prerequisite to the revocation of bail on the basis of alleged offenses committed while defendant was released on bail or personal recognizance. The court further held that Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 276, § 58 gave defendants the right to de novo review of district court bail determinations, including subsequent modifications or revisions, by the superior court. However, the court held that § 58 was not intended to provide similar de novo review by the superior court of bail revocation orders, reasoning that review of a bail revocation hearing was more in the nature of an appeal than a de novo determination. The court affirmed the judgment of the single justice.


OUTCOME: Although the case was moot, the court heard the appeal to resolve the issues raised because they were likely to arise again yet evade review by becoming moot. The court held that the superior court did not have jurisdiction to consider an appeal of a district court decision revoking bail on the basis of a crime being committed when defendant was released on bail or on his own recognizance. The court affirmed the judgment of the single justice.

 

125 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


American Trucking Ass'ns, Inc. v. Secretary of Admin.


S-6054


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


415 Mass. 337; 613 N.E.2d 95; 1993 Mass. LEXIS 281


February 4, 1993, Argued  
May 25, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on October 21, 1991. The case was reported to the Appeals Court by Hiller B. Zobel, J., on a statement of agreed facts. The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct review.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, trucking association and interstate trucking companies, brought a class action against the commonwealth, and alleged that certain annual fuel license fees, and a hazardous waste fee, were assessed by the commonwealth in a manner that violated the Commerce Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8. The court granted the trucking association's application for direct appellate review.


OVERVIEW: The commonwealth assessed a "User of Special Fuels License," that was required for each vehicle operated in Massachusetts which used diesel or other non-gasoline fuels, Mass. Regs. Code tit. 801, § 4.02 (830) (1), (3) (1989); a "Motor Carrier Tax Vehicle License," that was required for each vehicle operated in Massachusetts by a licensed motor carrier which used any type of fuel purchased or acquired outside of Massachusetts; and a transportation of hazardous waste fee under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 21C, § 7, para. 5 (1990). On appeal, the court applied the internal consistency test, which required that a state tax that applied to interstate business be of a kind that, if applied by every jurisdiction, there would be no impermissible interference with free trade. Here, the court held that each of the fees failed the test, and each was in violation of the Commerce Clause of the United States Constitution. The fees discriminated against out-of-state truckers by subjecting them to a higher charge per mile traveled in Massachusetts, and did not fairly approximate the value of any benefit received or a cost actually incurred in the commonwealth.


OUTCOME: The court declared that the three challenged fees were unconstitutional under the Commerce Clause of the United States Constitution, and the commonwealth was enjoined from collecting the fees until a constitutionally permissible method of assessing them was determined. The action was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with the opinion, including, among others, the questions of damages and attorney's fees.

 

126 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Tsagronis v. Board of Appeals


P-6046


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


415 Mass. 329; 613 N.E.2d 893; 1993 Mass. LEXIS 279


December 7, 1992, Argued  
May 24, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Plymouth. Civil action action commenced in the Superior Court Department on December 15, 1989. The case was heard by Suzanne V. DelVecchio, J., on motions for summary judgment. After review by the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court granted leave to obtain further appellate review.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property abutters sought review of the decision from the Appeals Court (Massachusetts), which affirmed the grant of a variance to defendant property owners that allowed the property owners to construct a house on a lot with inadequate frontage.


OVERVIEW: A subdivision was approved by the city and prior to houses being built the city increased the frontage requirements for lots in the district. The subdivision granted an exemption to the lots and houses were erected on all but one of the lots. The owners of the vacant lot applied for a variance to construct a house on the lot and the abutters objected. The board of appeals granted the variance, finding that the exemption period had expired, and the lower court affirmed the issuance of the variance. The abutters challenged the decision and the court reversed. Under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 40A, § 10 (1990 ed.) variances could only be granted if circumstances relating to the soil conditions of the land, the shape of the land, or topography of the land caused hardship to the owners. Inadequate frontage did not qualify as "shape of the land" or satisfy the statutory requirement of hardship and could not be the basis for granting a variance. The hardship was due solely to the fact that the owners failed to construct a house before the statutory protections against the zoning changes ran out.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of a zoning variance to the property owners.

 

127 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Murphy v. Commissioner of Dep't of Indus. Accidents


S-6063


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


415 Mass. 218; 612 N.E.2d 1149; 1993 Mass. LEXIS 272


November 3, 1992, Argued  
May 12, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on July 23, 1992. A motion for preliminary injunctive relief was heard by Robert Malcolm Graham, J. A request for interlocutory review was heard in the Appeals Court by Kenneth Laurence, J. The Supreme Judicial Court transferred the case on its own initiative.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff spouse challenged a decision of the Superior Court (Massachusetts), which denied plaintiff's request for a preliminary injunction regarding her challenge of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 152, § 11A in a workmen's compensation suit against defendant Commissioner of the Department of Industrial Accidents.


OVERVIEW: In an action for declaratory and injunctive relief, plaintiff spouse challenged the constitutionality of the fee provisions of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 152, § 11A in a case involving defendant Commissioner of the Department of Industrial Accidents. The challenge came after plaintiff's request for a preliminary injunction was denied in a workers' compensation case brought on behalf of plaintiff's deceased husband. The court ordered declaratory judgment and held that the challenged portions violated the equal protection clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights amend. art. 11. The court was unable to ascertain any rational basis for the imposition of a filing fee only on litigants proceeding with the assistance of counsel and found that the relationship of the presently challenged classification to any goal was so attenuated as to render the distinction arbitrary or irrational. The classification merely penalized claimants who chose to engage counsel and singled out these claimants for "arbitrary and capricious" treatment.


OUTCOME: The court ordered declaratory judgment for plaintiff spouse in her challenge of a fee provision statute in a case involving defendant Commissioner of the Department of Industrial Accidents. The court held that there was no rational basis for imposition of a filing fee only on litigants proceeding with the assistance of counsel.

 

128 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Cambridge v. Phillips


M-6080


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


415 Mass. 126; 612 N.E.2d 638; 1993 Mass. LEXIS 259


January 7, 1993, Argued  
May 4, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Middlesex. Traffic citation issued on May 25, 1990. The case was heard in the Cambridge Division of the District Court Department by Herbert H. Hershfang, J. The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of an appellate court (Massachusetts), which affirmed the judgment of the district court and magistrate, which found defendant responsible for a traffic violation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped for making an illegal left turn. In offenses of that type, the officer had the option of giving a warning or issuing a citation. Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 90C, § 3(A). The officer issued a citation to defendant. Defendant argued that ch. 90C, § 3(A) was unconstitutionally vague because it gave officers no guidance as to when they should issue a warning and when they should issue a citation. The trial court found defendant responsible for the violation, and the judgment was affirmed by the district and appellate courts. On further review, the court held that a statute could be void for vagueness if it impermissibly delegated basic policy matters to policemen, judges or juries for resolution on an ad hoc and subjective basis. The court held that the violation was a civil matter for which the maximum penalty was the payment of a fine; however, payment of the fine operated as a conviction for purposes of driver registry and insurance. The court held that the option to issue a warning or a citation was not impermissibly vague and that it was proper for police to have some disruption in whether or not to issue a citation. The court affirmed the appellate court's judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's judgment which affirmed the findings that defendant was responsible for the traffic violation.

West Lynn Creamery v. Commissioner of Dep't of Food & Agric.


S-6140


SUPREME JUDICIAL COURT OF MASSACHUSETTS


415 Mass. 8; 611 N.E.2d 239; 1993 Mass. LEXIS 199


January 6, 1993, Argued  
April 15, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk. Civil actions commenced in the Superior Court Department, one on July 24, 1992, and two on November 18, 1992. Motions for preliminary injunctive relief were heard by R. Malcolm Graham, J., and John L. Murphy, Jr., J., respectively. After the latter two cases were reported to the Appeals Court by J. Harold Flannery, J., the proceedings were consolidated for hearing in that court. The Supreme Judicial Court transferred them on its own initiative.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff milk dealers filed suit against defendant, Commissioner of the Department of Food and Agriculture (commissioner) to challenge his revocation of their milk dealers' licenses due to their failure to comply with a pricing order. An preliminary injunction was granted to the milk dealers. The parties agreed to interlocutory relief from a panel of the Appeals Court (Massachusetts). The court transferred the cases on its own motion.


OVERVIEW: In order to combat a perceived state of emergency in the commonwealth's dairy industry, the commissioner issued an amended pricing order pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws. ch. 94A, §§ 10-12. The order set forth a plan designed to boost the amount of money local dairy farmers, the producers, received for milk above and beyond that required by a federal program. The order required milk dealers to submit monthly reports and to contribute to a state equalization fund. The commissioner distributed the fund to producers in proportion to the milk produced in the commonwealth during the preceding month. The milk dealers failed to comply with the pricing order, and the commissioner revoked their milk dealers' licenses. The milk dealers filed suit, arguing that the pricing order violated the Commerce Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, because the order denied out-of-state milk producers the opportunity to compete with in-state milk producers because of the commonwealth's premium. On appeal, the court disagreed, holding that the order was constitutional because it had a merely incidental burden on interstate commerce. The court then remanded the case for further action.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the cases to the superior court for action not inconsistent with its opinion.

Aime v. Commonwealth


S-6089


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


414 Mass. 667; 611 N.E.2d 204; 1993 Mass. LEXIS 179


December 8, 1992, Argued  
April 5, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on October 27, 1992.

The case was reported by Wilkins, J.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was arrested. Bail was set in the amount of $ 100,000 cash or $ 1,000,000 surety. The Supreme Judicial Court for the County of Suffolk (Massachusetts) found that such a bail was in accordance with the requirements of due process. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that a state bail statute, which authorized an official to refuse to release a prisoner in the exercise of his discretion, violated the due process clause of the Fourteenth Amendment because the statute infringed on defendant's fundamental right to be free from arbitrary governmental detention. Defendant also argued that the amendment did not provide sufficient procedural safeguards against an erroneous deprivation of liberty. The State argued that the statute did not create a preventative statutory scheme. The court determined that the statute infringed on defendant's interest in freedom from detention. The amendment essentially granted a judicial officer unbridled discretion to determine whether an arrested individual was dangerous. The court determined that such a statute did not comply with the federal Bail Reform Act. Furthermore, the court determined that the challenged portions of the statute did not comport with due process of law under the Fourteenth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the cause for entry of a judgment consistent with this opinion.

Massachusetts Wholesalers of Malt Beverages, Inc. v. Commonwealth


S-5934


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


414 Mass. 411; 609 N.E.2d 67; 1993 Mass. LEXIS 78


November 5, 1992, Argued  
March 1, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on January 26, 1990.

On transfer to the Superior Court Department, the case was heard by Charles F. Barrett, J., on motions for summary judgment and was reported by him to the Appeals Court. The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct review.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Direct appellate review was granted as to a decision from the Superior Court for Suffolk County (Massachusetts), which allowed in part and denied in part the parties' cross-motions for summary judgment as to plaintiff bottle wholesalers' action for declaratory and injunctive relief on claims that defendant commonwealth's amended bottle bill, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 94, §§ 321- 327, violated the takings clauses of the state and federal constitutions.


OVERVIEW: The trial judge had ruled that the amendment, apart from the retroactive funding portion, did not effect a taking of any private property, did not violate any constitutional requirement concerning abandoned property, and was a proper exercise of legislative power establishing that refund values belong to consumers until they escheated to the state. However, the retroactive funding provision in 1989 Mass. Acts ch. 653, § 237 effected an unconstitutional retroactive taking of the property as to refund values collected during the three months prior to the amendment's effective date, although the provision was severable. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding no violation of the takings clause by conferring the right to the deposits on the consumer and, once abandoned, on the state, as rights created under the original bottle bill did not translate into a similar set of rights under the amended bill. The court agreed that the retroactive funding provision unconstitutionally directed the taking of the private property without compensation; however, as it was severable from the rest of the amendment, the remainder of the amendment's abandoned property scheme was not improper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the partial granting and partial denial of the cross-motions for summary judgment as to the constitutionality of the challenged provisions of the commonwealth's amended "bottle bill."

Local 589, Amalgamated Transit Union v. Massachusetts Bay Transp. Authority


S-6056


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


414 Mass. 323; 607 N.E.2d 1011; 1993 Mass. LEXIS 30; 16 Employee Benefits Cas. (BNA) 1864; 142 L.R.R.M. 2749


November 5, 1992, Argued  
February 16, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Superior Court Department on October 31, 1991.

The case was reported to the Appeals Court by Hiller B. Zobel, J., on a statement of agreed facts. The Supreme Judicial Court transferred the case on its own initiative.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff union brought an action against defendant Massachusetts Bay Transportation Authority in the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts), seeking a declaration of its rights and an injunction against the authority's implementation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 161A, § 19J (1991), which required that employees contribute toward the cost of health insurance.


OVERVIEW: The parties' collective bargaining agreement, which provided that the authority was to pay the entire cost of health insurance, also stated that its provisions continued until changed by agreement. The court ordered that judgment be entered declaring that the provisions of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 161A, § 19J did not apply to the collective bargaining agreement between the union and the authority because there was no indication that the legislature intended the employee contribution mandate of § 19J to apply to a collective bargaining agreement that was in effect on the effective date of that mandate. Where a strike would be unlawful, or at least arguably so, and arbitration was mandated for the ultimate resolution of disputes concerning the collective bargaining agreement's terms, public policy supported the enforcement of the collective bargaining agreement as written and the rejection of any implication of a right to terminate it on reasonable notice.


OUTCOME: The court ordered that a judgment be entered declaring that the employee contribution provisions did not apply to the parties' collective bargaining agreement. The court did not grant the union's request for injunctive relief because it concluded the authority would comply with the judgment.

Commonwealth v. Wayne W.


S-6008


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


414 Mass. 218; 606 N.E.2d 1323; 1993 Mass. LEXIS 19


October 6, 1992, Argued  
January 27, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] INDICTMENTS found and returned in the Superior Court Department on November 22, 1991.

Motions to dismiss were heard by John F. Moriarty, J., and the cases were reported by him to the Appeals Court. The Supreme Judicial Court transferred the case on its own initiative.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, juveniles accused of murder charges, filed a motion seeking to dismiss the indictments on the ground that the new Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 119, § 61 (1990), under which they were transferred for trial as adults, was unconstitutional and on the ground that their expert psychiatric testimony was improperly excluded as a sanction. The state's highest court transferred the cases on its own initiative.


OVERVIEW: The juveniles, who were both charged in connection with two murders, moved to dismiss the indictments on the ground that the new Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 119, § 61 (1990), under which they were transferred for trial as adults, violated state and federal constitutional provisions. The juveniles also argued that the Juvenile Court judge erred in excluding their expert psychiatric testimony as a sanction for failure to cooperate in court-ordered examinations. Concluding that a serious issue as to the constitutional validity of the statute was raised, the trial court certified the motions to an appeals court. The state's highest court transferred the case on its own initiative. Upon review, the state's highest court concluded that the statute was constitutional because the legislative distinction between charges of delinquency by reason of murder and delinquency by reason of other crimes was a rational one. However, the state's highest court held that the issue of admission of expert psychiatric evidence must be reconsidered because while the self-incrimination privilege applied, the juveniles could be ordered to submit to an exam if they chose to offer expert psychiatric evidence.


OUTCOME: The court concluded that the lower court's conclusion that the statute was constitutional was correct and that the motions to dismiss on those grounds were to be denied. The court, however, held that the juveniles must be allowed to decide whether they wished to offer their expert psychiatric testimony in view of the court's conclusion that, if they planned to do so, they could be made to undergo examinations by the commonwealth's expert.

 

134 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Spano


P-5979


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Plymouth


414 Mass. 178; 605 N.E.2d 1241; 1993 Mass. LEXIS 14


October 8, 1992, Argued  
January 15, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected March 31, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: INDICTMENTS found and returned in the Superior Court Department on February 28, 1990.

A pretrial motion to suppress evidence was considered by Cortland A. Mathers, J., and the cases were heard by John M. Xifaras, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions in the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts) for trafficking in cocaine, possession of cocaine with intent to distribute while within 1,000 feet of a school, and possession of cocaine with intent to distribute, and appealed the denial of his motion to suppress evidence seized and statements made during and subsequent to the execution of a search warrant, arguing that it was not supported by probable cause.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial judge erred in denying his motion for a required finding of not guilty, based on a claim that Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 94C, § 32J was unconstitutionally vague in that it did not proscribe how to measure the distance from a school. On appeal, the court found no error in the finding that the distance between defendant's house and a school was less than the proscribed distance of 1,000 feet. As to defendant's probable cause argument, the court found that affidavits based on information from confidential informants were required by Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights art. 14 to inform a magistrate of the underlying circumstances of an informant's basis of knowledge and his or her reliability or veracity. The court found that the affidavit supporting the warrant in question satisfied both prongs of the test. The informants' observations satisfied the basis of knowledge test, and independent police corroboration of the informants' information satisfied the veracity test. Further, the informants' statements were a declaration against their penal interests and established credibility. The court affirmed the convictions and the denial of the motion to suppress.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion to suppress, and affirmed his convictions for trafficking in cocaine, possession of cocaine with intent to distribute while within 1,000 feet of a school, and possession of cocaine with intent to distribute.

In re Rhode Island Grand Jury Subpoena


M-6039


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Middlesex


414 Mass. 104; 605 N.E.2d 840; 1993 Mass. LEXIS 3


October 8, 1992, Argued  
January 8, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] MOTION filed in the Superior Court Department on May 22, 1992.

The proceeding was heard by John P. Forte, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Prosecutor for foreign state sought review of stay of execution granted by a justice of the Massachusetts Appeals Court after the motion judge of the trial court denied the requests by the investigated person to quash the subpoena issued by a Rhode Island court and to stay the order by the trial court directing the accountant of the investigated person to submit the requested documents to the Rhode Island grand jury.


OVERVIEW: A Rhode Island grand jury issued two subpoenas duces tecum to an accountant of the investigated person. The accountant was willing to deliver the documents requested by the grand jury in Rhode Island, but the investigated person objected. The motion judge of the trial court denied the investigated person's motions to quash the subpoena or stay the order of the trial court directing the accountant to provide the documents. One justice of the court of appeals stayed the execution of the trial court's order. The court vacated the appeals court stay and affirmed the trial court's order directing production by the accountant. The court found that the investigated person lacked standing to intervene to move to quash the subpoena served on his accountant--only the accountant could challenge the subpoena. The court also concluded that in determining the materiality and necessity of a witness consistent with the Uniform Law to Secure the Attendance of Witnesses from Without a State in Criminal Proceedings, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 233, §§ 13A-13D (1990), a Massachusetts court could rely on another state's certificate statement that an in-state witness was material.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the stay issued by a justice of the appeals court and affirmed the ruling of the motion judge of the trial court denying the investigated person's request to stay the trial court's order directing the accountant of the investigated person to surrender the subpoenaed documents and denying the motion to quash the Rhode Island subpoena. The court held that the investigated person lacked standing to challenge the subpoena.

 

136 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Steinbergh v. Cambridge


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Middlesex


413 Mass. 736; 604 N.E.2d 1269; 1992 Mass. LEXIS 586


September 15, 1992  
December 10, 1992 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Superior Court Department on February 9, 1990.

The case was heard by Wendie I. Gershengorn, J., on motions for summary judgment.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners appealed the summary judgment of the Superior Court of Middlesex County (Massachusetts), entered in favor of defendant city on plaintiffs' claim that defendant's application of a challenged ordinance constituted an uncompensated, temporary regulatory taking of property.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff property owners sought an award of damages against defendant city, claiming that defendant's unlawful restriction on their right to sell individual condominium units was unconstitutional and deprived them, to their financial detriment, of the right to sell individual units for over two years. The trial court rejected defendant's argument that plaintiffs were barred by an earlier judgment from presenting their constitutionally-based claim for damages, but agreed with defendant that its conduct did not amount to a taking or to a denial of due process or equal protection of the laws. On appeal the court affirmed, holding that the challenged regulation did not interfere with plaintiffs' investment-based expectations. Plaintiffs acquired the property when the regulation was already in effect. The price that they paid for the property should have reflected any adverse impact the regulation had on the fair market value of the property. The fact that plaintiffs could not make immediate optimum use of their property and thus were unable to sell the units at prices higher than those at which they could sell them after the regulation was invalidated did not constitute a taking.


OUTCOME: The summary judgment in favor of defendant city on plaintiff property owners' claim that defendant's application of a restriction on plaintiffs' property rights amounted to a taking without just compensation was affirmed. The application of the regulation that was struck down did not interfere with plaintiffs' investment-based expectations because they bought the properties when the regulation was in effect.
