Commonwealth v. Caceres


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Worcester


413 Mass. 749; 604 N.E.2d 677; 1992 Mass. LEXIS 587


September 15, 1992  
December 10, 1992 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] INDICTMENT found and returned in the Superior Court Department on November 8, 1990.

A pretrial motion to suppress evidence was heard by Robert V. Mulkern, J., and the case was tried before Richard F. Connon, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court (Massachusetts), which convicted defendant of trafficking in cocaine.


OVERVIEW: A state trooper stopped the vehicle defendant was driving and then arrested defendant for giving him a false name. Cocaine was later discovered in defendant's seized vehicle during an inventory search of the vehicle. Defendant was indicted on charges of trafficking in cocaine and his motion to suppress the evidence seized during the inventory search was denied. Defendant was convicted of the trafficking charges and sought review. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction, holding that the police had a right to conduct the inventory search because there was no practical available alternative to the removal of the vehicle and to an inventory search of it. There was no person present to drive away the vehicle except a passenger, who had no valid driver's license. The court held that the inclusion of the bag containing the cocaine, which was located in the trunk, in the inventory search was permissible because the bag was located in an accessible storage area. The court further held that U.S. Const. amend. IV and Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights art. 14 were not violated by the opening of a closed container pursuant to standard inventory procedures.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant of trafficking in cocaine because the inventory search of defendant's vehicle in which the police discovered the cocaine was constitutional.

 

138 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Dugan v. Board of Selectman


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Bristol


413 Mass. 641; 602 N.E.2d 563; 1992 Mass. LEXIS 545


September 14, 1992  
November 6, 1992 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Superior Court Department on July 6, 1990.

The case was heard by William H. Carey, J., and a motion for an award of attorney's fees was considered by him.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff police officer sought review from an order of the Superior Court of Massachusetts, which denied him attorneys' fees in a suit against defendant town, involving indemnification arising out of a claim against the police officer.


OVERVIEW: A suit was commenced against the officer and others for malicious prosecution and damages were assessed. The officer was entitled to indemnification for attorneys' fees arising out of the federal action against him. The question was whether attorneys' fees incurred to enforce a statutory right of indemnification were fees for which the legislature intended people like the officer to be indemnified. The court held that the officer's legal fees and expenses arose out of the federal suit within the intent of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 258, § 13 (1990 ed.), and, therefore, he should have been indemnified for legal fees and expenses he incurred in order that he be made whole. By accepting § 13, the town agreed to pay the judgment and costs of defense. It was thus required to pay for the consequences of its failure to do so. The court adopted a rule that encouraged municipalities with a duty to indemnify to do so promptly. The rule attempted to assure that all municipal officers protected by § 13 would be treated equally. The order that denied counsel fees was vacated and the case was remanded to the lower court.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order that denied counsel fees and remanded the case to the lower court.

 

139 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. Boston


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


413 Mass. 607; 602 N.E.2d 198; 1992 Mass. LEXIS 538


October 5, 1992  
November 5, 1992 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Superior Court Department on December 3, 1987.

The case was tried before Mel L. Greenberg, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee appealed the judgment of a Massachusetts superior court which held that defendant city was not liable to the employee for a violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and directed a verdict in favor of the city. On its own initiative, the Supreme Judicial Court transferred the matter from the Massachusetts Appeals Court to itself.


OVERVIEW: The city's director of personnel fired the employee for abusive reasons and violated the city's policies that employees were to be fairly treated. The mayor was the chief executive officer of the city, and Boston, Mass., Rev. Ordinances tit. 5, § 5-1.2, provided that the director only made recommendations to the mayor concerning personnel matters. The lower court held that the employee had failed to state a § 1983 claim against the city, and the court affirmed. The court held that the director was not a final policy making authority with regard to personnel matters and had violated the city's policies against unfair treatment. Because there was no custom or unofficial policy justifying the director's abusive treatment of the employee, the city was not liable. Even if the mayor had acquiesced in the director's actions, there was no evidence that the mayor ratified the director's actions. Therefore, the city was not responsible to the employee under § 1983.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court, which held that the city was not liable to the employee under § 1983 for a director of personnel's abusive termination of the employee.

 

140 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Wilson v. Commonwealth


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Barnstable


413 Mass. 352; 597 N.E.2d 43; 1992 Mass. LEXIS 446


May 4, 1992  
August 11, 1992 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Superior Court Department on July 31, 1989.

The case was heard by James J. Nixon, J., on a motion to dismiss.

After review by the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court granted leave to obtain further appellate review.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant commonwealth sought review of the decision of an appeals court (Massachusetts), which affirmed the trial court's dismissal of plaintiff property owners' complaint except as to the counts of the complaint that alleged a taking. The property owners' complaint had alleged that the commonwealth had acted negligently and unlawfully and had made a regulatory taking of their properties.


OVERVIEW: The property owners had commenced administrative proceedings that sought permission to erect protective barriers to have prevented erosion of their properties. While the property owners' administrative appeal was pending, their houses were destroyed by the sea. The commonwealth argued that the circumstances disclosed by the pleadings could not have constituted a regulatory taking. The court reversed the judgment on the taking claim and remanded the case for further proceedings. In all other respects the judgment was affirmed. The court concluded that the complaint in one respect stated a claim of a regulatory taking that was sufficient to have survived a motion to dismiss. The property owners' claims did not fail in all respects simply because the administrative process was not completed before the properties were made worthless. The property owners' claim that if there had been no improper delays in the agency proceedings, their property would not have been damaged as a result, and the court determined that that claim was adequately alleged in the generality of the complaint.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment on the taking claim and remanded the matter for further, consistent proceedings. The remainder of the judgment was affirmed.

 

141 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Mitchell v. Secretary of Admin.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


413 Mass. 330; 597 N.E.2d 400; 1992 Mass. LEXIS 442


May 6, 1992  
August 10, 1992 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on September 19, 1991.

The case was reported by Wilkins, J.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, individual taxpayers and citizen groups (taxpayers), challenged the legality of a transfer made by defendant comptroller of money from the highway fund to the general fund in order to balance the commonwealth's books for fiscal year 1991. The taxpayers sought a declaration that the transfer violated Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights art. 78. A single justice reserved and reported the action to the full court.


OVERVIEW: In 1991, the Massachusetts legislature passed legislation that transferred revenues that were credited to the highway fund to the general fund to offset a deficit. A portion of the general fund revenues had been spent on transportation related purposes. The taxpayers challenged the transaction on the grounds that it violated the Massachusetts Constitution, specifically that revenue allocated to the highway fund could not be used for items delineated in the general fund. The court held that the transfer of funds did not violate Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights art. 78, when art. 78 only required that the revenues generated from vehicle and license fees be spent on transportation related purposes. It did not matter under art. 78 where the art. 78 revenues were designated. The court held that there was no constitutional limitation on the legislature to amend a prior act of appropriation. The court held that the categorization of certain highway fund revenues as "undesignated" and thus available for transfer was appropriate. The court ordered the matter remanded for an order that the declaration of the transfer between funds was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the matter for entry of an order finding the challenged legislation that transferred money between two of the commonwealths' operating funds to be proper.

 

142 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Lydon


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


413 Mass. 309; 597 N.E.2d 36; 1992 Mass. LEXIS 405


May 7, 1992  
July 29, 1992 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] INDICTMENTS found and returned in the Superior Court Department on November 15, 1985.

The cases were tried before Robert V. Mulkern, J., and a motion for a new trial was heard by him.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts), which convicted defendant for murder in the first degree and unlawful possession of a firearm. After defendant filed postconviction motions for a new trial, for interviews of jurors, and an amended motion based on ineffective assistance of counsel, the court remanded the motions to the trial court. The trial court ultimately denied the motions.


OVERVIEW: On appeal for a second time, the court affirmed defendant's conviction for unlawful possession of a firearm. However, the court reversed the conviction for murder in the first degree and remanded the cause for a new trial. In pertinent part, the court held that defendant's argument in a footnote that the evidence was insufficient to convict him of unlawful possession of a firearm was deemed waived because arguments relegated to a footnote did not rise to the level of appellate argument. Nevertheless, on a review of the issue, the court concluded that the evidence was sufficient to warrant the conviction. On the other hand, the court held that the trial court erred by allowing the state to introduce evidence of defendant's refusal to have his hands swabbed. The court held that although the issue was not clearly raised at trial, the error created a substantial likelihood of a miscarriage of justice on the murder conviction. The court held that the refusal of evidence should not have been admitted because its use violated defendant's privilege against self-incrimination secured by Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights art. 12.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the defendant's conviction for unlawful possession of a firearm, but reversed the conviction for murder in the first degree. The court remanded the cause for a new trial.

Rushworth v. Registrar of Motor Vehicles


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


413 Mass. 265; 596 N.E.2d 340; 1992 Mass. LEXIS 403


May 5, 1992  
July 27, 1992

The case was reported to the Appeals Court by Elbert Tuttle, J., on a statement of agreed facts. The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct review.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff drivers with suspended licenses filed an action seeking declaratory and injunctive relief in the Superior Court (Massachusetts) against defendant Registrar of Motor Vehicles (registrar). The court granted the drivers' application for direct appellate review.


OVERVIEW: Certain drivers filed an action in the superior court against the registrar seeking declaratory and injunctive relief. On application for direct appellate review, the drivers challenged the validity of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 90, § 22(f) (1989), on due process, equal protection, and double jeopardy grounds. The court determined that the statute, which required the registrar to automatically suspend the driver's license of a person convicted of violating the Controlled Substance Act, had a reasonable relationship to a permissible legislative objective, rationally furthered legitimate state objectives, and did not implicate double jeopardy principles.


OUTCOME: The court rejected the drivers' challenges and directed the entry of a declaratory judgment upholding the statute, which automatically suspended their drivers' license based on a conviction under the Controlled Substances Act.

 

144 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Taylor


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


413 Mass. 243; 596 N.E.2d 333; 1992 Mass. LEXIS 398


May 6, 1992  
July 24, 1992 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] COMPLAINT received and sworn to in the Boston Municipal Court Department on October 23, 1989.

On appeal to the jury session of that court, a motion to dismiss was heard by Theodore S. Bakas, J., and the case was tried before him.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Boston Municipal Court Department (Massachusetts), which convicted him of possession of marihuana with intent to distribute in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 94C, § 32C after he had already entered a guilty plea in the primary session, and also convicted him of possession of marihuana with intent to distribute within 1,000 feet of a school in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 94C, § 32J.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was charged with possession of marihuana with intent to distribute, § 32C, and possession of marihuana with intent to distribute within 1,000 feet of a school, § 32J, he was convicted in the primary session on the § 32C offense and sought a jury trial on the § 32J offense. Due to a procedural error, he was retried on both offenses in the jury session and found guilty. Defendant appealed. The court affirmed the § 32J conviction, but reversed the § 32C conviction, holding that because defendant did not appeal the § 32C conviction from the primary session, that conviction stood and had to be reinstated. Double jeopardy did not apply because the retrial was of no legal significance with respect to the de novo trial of the § 32J offense. Section 32J was not vague because it did not encourage arbitrary and discriminatory enforcement. Further, the statute was not overbroad because it did not prohibit constitutionally protected conduct. Defendant's claim of ineffective assistance of counsel was without merit because counsel's concession of the possession charge was a tactical decision to press the defense that there was no intent to distribute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for possession of marihuana with intent to distribute within 1,000 feet of a school. The court vacated defendant's conviction in the jury session for possession of marihuana with intent to distribute, and it ordered that his conviction as entered in the primary session be reinstated..

OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions of unlawful possession of heroin with intent to distribute and of the unlawful possession of heroin with intent to distribute while within 1,000 feet of a school.

Commonwealth v. Grimshaw


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Middlesex


413 Mass. 73; 595 N.E.2d 302; 1992 Mass. LEXIS 388


March 5, 1992  
July 9, 1992 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended July 27, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: COMPLAINT received and sworn to in the Cambridge Division of the District Court Department on December 21, 1990.

On appeal to the jury session of that division, a motion to suppress evidence was heard by Mark E. Lawton, J., sitting under statutory authority.

An application for an interlocutory appeal was allowed by Greaney, J., in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk and the appeal was reported by him to the Appeals Court. The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the matter from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Order denying the defendant's motion to suppress affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Cambridge Division of the District Court Department (Massachusetts), which convicted defendant of possession with intent to have distributed a class A substance and knowingly having been present where heroin was kept, and denied defendant's motion to suppress.


OVERVIEW: A search was executed at 8:50 p.m. when the search warrant prohibited its execution at any time during the night. Defendant argued that the search was conducted in violation of the warrant's express prohibition against a nighttime search and therefore the evidence should have been suppressed. The court disagreed and affirmed the judgment. The court held that the circumstances did not require the suppression of the evidence. The court determined that the prohibition of a nighttime search was intended as a safeguard against abusive, arbitrary action on the part of the police. The procedural letter and not the substantive spirit of the law was violated. The court further determined that suppression would not have deterred future police misconduct. Finally, the court held that for warrant purposes, nighttime began at 10 p.m. and ended at 6 a.m., as articulated in Fed. R. Crim. P. 41(h).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and also the trial court's denial of defendant's motion to suppress.

[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Middlesex


412 Mass. 790; 593 N.E.2d 222; 1992 Mass. LEXIS 326


February 3, 1992  
June 9, 1992

The case was heard by Gordon L. Doerfer, J., on a motion for summary judgment.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff recipients of aid to families with dependent children (AFDC recipients) challenged the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts) partial summary judgment in favor of defendant Commissioner of Public Welfare (commissioner) in an action challenging the constitutionality of 1990 Mass Acts ch. 150, § 58 and Mass. Regs. Code tit. 106 § 304.305(b). They alleged federal preemption and denial of equal protection.


OVERVIEW: The AFDC recipients initiated an action against the commissioner seeking injunctive and declaratory relief on the basis that 1990 Mass. Acts ch. 150, § 58 and Mass. Regs. Code tit. 106 § 304.305(b) violated federal laws and denied them equal protection. They alleged that the requirement to add non-siblings residing with a nonparent to the "assistance unit" of a grantee relative deprived them of the AFDC grant they would receive as an independent unit. The trial court granted partial summary judgment to the commissioner and the AFDC recipients appealed, asserting that the state scheme was preempted by federal laws and was unconstitutional. The court affirmed, ruling that because the federal AFDC statutory scheme envisioned state participation in implementing the program, the AFDC recipients' preemption argument failed. Further, they had not presented any clear and unambiguous statement preempting 1990 Mass. Acts ch. 150, § 58. The court discerned no congressional intent prohibiting the state from consolidating assistance units in the manner established by § 58. It held that neither § 58 nor the regulation violated equal protection provisions of federal and state constitutions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the partial summary judgment in favor of the commissioner in the AFDC recipients' action to enjoin the state AFDC scheme as unconstitutional and violative of federal laws.

Handy v. Penal Inst. Comm'r

A motion for an award of attorneys' fees was heard by Liacos, C.J.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, Penal Institutions Commissioner of Boston and other city officials, appealed from a judgment, entered by a single justice of the court, awarding attorneys' fees to plaintiff inmates in their class action, which was based in part on claims of violations of constitutional rights protected under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The inmates appealed from the justice's decision to reduce the amount of the fees they claimed.


OVERVIEW: Defendants argued that defects in the inmates complaint barred recovery of attorneys' fees under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988 and that attorneys' fees may not have been awarded under § 1988 because the action was not a cause of improvements that defendants made in the house of correction, and the documentation submitted in support of the award of attorneys' fees did not justify the award of the fees allowed. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders concerning attorneys' fees.

American Motorcyclist Ass'n v. Park Com. of Brockton


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Plymouth


412 Mass. 753; 592 N.E.2d 1314; 1992 Mass. LEXIS 319


February 6, 1992  
June 5, 1992 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Superior Court Department on September 30, 1987.

The case was heard by John M. Xifaras, J., on a statement of agreed facts, and a motion for relief from judgment was also heard by him.

After review by the Appeals Court, the Supreme Judicial Court granted leave to obtain further appellate review.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff association sought review of a judgment of the Appeals Court (Massachusetts), which affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The trial court entered judgment in favor of defendant park commission (commission). The association filed an action against the commission seeking an injunction against its enforcement of a regulation banning the use of motorized cycles on roadways and other areas under the commission's jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: The city park in question had approximately six miles of roadways. The park roads were not public ways, but the public had a right of access to them. The commission adopted a regulation to prohibit the use of motorized cycles in city parks. The regulation prohibited the use of all two-, three-, and four-wheeled motorized cycles, specifically including motorcycles. The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which entered judgment in favor of the commission. The appellate court had affirmed the trial court. The case was remanded to the trial court for entry of declaratory and injunctive relief. The court held that the regulation conflicted with the statutory right to operate motor vehicles on the ways of the commonwealth, as established by the legislature in Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 90. The commission was not allowed to adopt a regulation that conflicted with state law. The commission was a municipal department of the city, and municipalities were not able to adopt by-laws or ordinances that were inconsistent with state law. Thus, the regulation was invalid.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which entered judgment in favor of the commission. The case was remanded to the trial court for entry of declaratory and injunctive relief.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landlord challenged the decision from the superior court (Massachusetts), which denied a declaratory judgment sought by the landlord that an attempt by the appellee town to control rents and evictions was invalid.


OVERVIEW: The landlord sought a declaration that rent controls adopted by the town were improper because the town had not enacted the rent control subject to a valid by-law. The trial court denied declaratory relief to the landlord because it determined that the rent control ordinance was valid. Opinion of Justices to Senate


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


412 Mass. 1201; 591 N.E.2d 1073; 1992 Mass. LEXIS 280


May 12, 1992  
May 12, 1992, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [***1] [NO DATA IN ORIGINAL]


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Senate of the Commonwealth of Massachusetts submitted a question to the Justices of the court regarding the constitutionality of a proposed bill, which would have amended Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 90, § 24(1)(3) (1990).


OVERVIEW: The Senate requested that the court determine whether a proposed statute, which would have permitted a defendant's failure or refusal to submit to a chemical test or analysis of his breath to be admissible as evidence in a criminal proceeding, would have violated the self-incrimination clause, Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights art. 12, in that the defendant would have been compelled to furnish evidence against himself. In answering in the affirmative, the court found that although some have said that the act of refusal was not a self-accusation, in the court's view it was simply wrong to conclude that refusal evidence used in the manner proposed was not evidence furnished by the accused. Therefore, such refusal evidence was both compelled and furnished evidence against oneself. The proposed statute therefore would have violated the privilege against self-incrimination of Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights art. 12.


OUTCOME: The court answered the question in the affirmative and found that the proposed statute would have violated the privilege against self-incrimination.

DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former employee sought review of a judgment by the Barnstable Division of the District Court Department (Massachusetts), which affirmed a decision of the board of review adopting the review examiner's decision affirming the denial of the employee's unemployment benefits by respondent Commissioner of the Department of Employment and Training's department.


OVERVIEW: Subsequent to the denial of the employee's unemployment benefits and the later affirmation of the denial of benefits, the employee appealed. The court noted that the findings and the decision of the board that the employee's entitlement to benefits depended on his meeting the minimum wage requirement of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 151A, § 24(a). The employee's total earnings, therefore, made him ineligible for unemployment compensation. The court further noted that the statute was not unconstitutional because the Legislature had a interest in providing unemployment benefits only for those working a certain predetermined minimum term. State legislatures were presumed to have acted within their constitutional power despite the fact that their laws resulted in some inequality.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's decision affirming the denial of unemployment benefits.

Massachusetts Hosp. Ass'n v. Department of Medical Sec.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]

412 Mass. 340; 588 N.E.2d 679; 1992 Mass. LEXIS 163


February 5, 1992

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff hospitals sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court (Massachusetts), which denied their request for an injunction compelling defendant Department of Medical Security (department) to conform the administration of the statewide uncompensated care pool for bad debt in accordance with a prior judgment that declared invalid Mass. Regs. Code tit. 117, § 204(4)(d), a regulation on debt collection practices.


OVERVIEW: The department maintained that its statutory grant of authority pursuant to Mass. Gen. The court found that the statute was intended to promote access to healthcare and gave complex formulas for determining the liability of the pool to the hospital and vice versa. The court noted that no deference was due when an agency's interpretation of a statute was incorrect, and found that the legislative history supported the hospitals' view that the statute required only that the hospital make a reasonable effort to collect payment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the hospitals and against the department, which declared the regulation invalid and unenforceable, and did not address the additional challenges to the regulation presented by the hospitals.

The case was reported to the Appeals Court by Hiller B. Zobel, J., on a statement of agreed facts. The Supreme Judicial Court transferred the case on its own initiative.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The trial court submitted a case on reservation and report in accordance with Mass. R. Civ. P. 64. The court, on its own motion, transferred the case to itself. The trial court reported the case on a statement of agreed facts between plaintiff securities firm and defendant tax commissioner in plaintiff's action for interpleader under Mass. R. Civ. P. 22 to determine the relative rights of defendant and plaintiff's account holders.


OVERVIEW: Defendant tax commissioner served two levies on plaintiff securities firm, which sought to reach the investment accounts an Illinois couple, who had failed to pay nonresident personal income taxes. Plaintiff brought an interpleader action under Mass. R. Civ. P. 22 to determine the relative rights of the parties. When the trial judge, pursuant to Mass. R. Civ. P. 64, reported the case on a statement of agreed facts, the court transferred the case to itself on its own motion. The court held that defendant had no authority to levy under Mass. Gen. The court concluded that plaintiff had standing because it had sufficient interest in the conflict between the interests of defendant and the interest of its account holders to entitle it to a declaratory judgment on that issue.


OUTCOME: The court entered a judgment that plaintiff securities firm did not hold in Massachusetts any property and rights to property subject to levy under state law because the account owners were Illinois residents.

Powers v. Secretary of Admin.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


412 Mass. 119; 587 N.E.2d 744; 1992 Mass. LEXIS 127


December 5, 1991  
March 4, 1992 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on September 17, 1991.

The case was reported by Wilkins, J., on a statement of agreed facts.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff homeowners filed a complaint against defendant Secretary of Administration, seeking a declaration that the Receivership Act, 1991 Mass. Acts 200, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The homeowners filed a complaint against the secretary, seeking a declaration that the Receivership Act (Act) was unconstitutional. The homeowners claimed that: (1) the legislature failed to meet the procedural requirements of § 8 of the Home Rule Amendment (Amendment) in passing the Act; and, (2) the legislature improperly delegated the implementation of the Act to the executive branch. On consideration, the court denied the homeowners' complaint for declaratory judgment. The court held that: (1) § 8 of the Amendment required only a two-thirds vote of each branch of the general court and did not require a roll call vote by the yeas and nays; and, (2) the legislature did not improperly delegate the implementation of the Act to the executive branch in violation of the state constitution. The legislature's decision, appointing a receiver to implement policy decisions that would improve the municipality's financial position, was not prohibited by the Amendment.


OUTCOME: The court denied the homeowners' complaint seeking a declaration that the legislature's decision appointing a receiver was unconstitutional.

 

156 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Oznemoc, Inc. v. Alcoholic Beverages Control Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


412 Mass. 100; 587 N.E.2d 751; 1992 Mass. LEXIS 96


December 3, 1991  
March 2, 1992 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Superior Court Department on September 20, 1989.

The case was heard by Barbara A. Dortch, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.

PETITION for a stay pending appeal filed in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on May 14, 1991.

The case was heard by Nolan, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated action, plaintiff license holder appealed the order of the Superior Court (Massachusetts), which affirmed the suspension of its liquor license by defendant, alcoholic beverages control commission (commission). The commission appealed the decision of a single justice of the court staying the enforcement of the suspension pending resolution of the license holder's appeal.


OVERVIEW: The liquor licensing board (board) heard charges against the license holder for violations of the liquor licensing law. Some of the violations stemmed from assaults on customers by an employee, which resulted in criminal charges against the employee. The board voted to revoke the license. The commission reduced the penalty to a 95-day suspension. The license holder appealed, but the trial court affirmed the commission's decision. The license holder appealed again and sought a stay pending the appeal. A single justice allowed the stay, and the commission appealed the order. After consolidating the appeals, the court affirmed both judgments and held that there was no evidence on the record to support the license holder's contention that it could not go forward in the administrative proceeding prior to the conclusion of the criminal charges pending against its employee. The license holder did not have standing to assert the employee's privilege against self-incrimination, and there was no violation of the license holder's due process rights. The commission's determinations were based on substantial evidence. The justice did not err in granting the stay pending appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's affirmance of the commission's suspension of the license holder's liquor license. The court also affirmed the grant of the request for a stay of the suspension pending the license holder's appeal.

 

157 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Opinion of Justices to Senate


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


413 Mass. 1201; 595 N.E.2d 292; 1992 Mass. LEXIS 377



1992, [NO DATE IN ORIGINAL]


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On July 7, 1992, the Justices submitted the following answers to questions propounded to them by the Senate.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Massachusetts Senate proposed questions as to the constitutionality of an initiative amendment, House Bill No. 4000, which proposed a term limitations amendment to the state constitution. The senate asked whether House Bill No. 4000 was inconsistent with the Declaration of Rights and was therefore excluded from the initiative process.


OVERVIEW: House Bill No. 4000 proposed term limitations on state elected officials. The senate asked the court whether the bill was inconsistent with Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights art. 9, and Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights amend. art. 48, § 2. The court found that it was not. Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights art. 9 provided that all inhabitants of the commonwealth, having such qualifications as they shall establish by their frame of government, have an equal right to elect officers, and to be elected, for public employment. The court found that the original draft contained a term limitation for the office of governor and that the ultimate vote against term limits had more to do with political compromises than with concern with rights provided by Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights art. 9. Therefore, the court held that House Bill No. 4000 was not inconsistent with the rights afforded by Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights art. 9 and was therefore not excluded from the initiative process by Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights amend. art. 48, § 2, which precluded the use of the initiative procedure to enact constitutional amendments inconsistent with the Declaration of Rights.


OUTCOME: The court concluded that House Bill No. 4000 was not inconsistent with the rights of individuals as presently declared in the Declaration of Rights, and was therefore not excluded from the initiative petition process.

Varga v. Board of Registration of Chiropractors


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


411 Mass. 302; 582 N.E.2d 492; 1991 Mass. LEXIS 569


October 7, 1991  
December 5, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected January 31, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on June 7, 1991.

The case was heard by Lynch, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant chiropractor sought further appellate review of a decision of a single justice of the Supreme Judicial Court (Massachusetts) affirming a decision of appellee Board of Registration of Chiropractors (board) suspending the chiropractor's license for six months and placing him on probation for two years.


OVERVIEW: The chiropractor alleged that the seven-member board lacked jurisdiction because it was not properly constituted, that one board member who participated in the decision should have recused himself, and that the decision rendered was not supported by substantial evidence. The court treated the jurisdictional challenge as a challenge to the validity of the board's action because it did not have two physician members as required by state law. The court found that, when the decision in the case at bar was issued, the law had been amended to eliminate the requirement in question. The court also held that, while due process did not require a professional disciplinary board member to recuse himself based upon his relationship with the insurance company that initiated the complaint, recusal might have been better practice. The court further held that its review of the record indicated that there was substantial evidence that the chiropractor engaged in overutilization of practice, assessed improper charges, and failed to provide a proper rationale for the use of certain procedures. The court, therefore, affirmed the decision suspending the chiropractor's license.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the single justice affirming the board's suspension of the chiropractor's license for six months, to be followed by two years of probation.

 

159 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Gordon v. Sheriff of Suffolk County


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


411 Mass. 238; 580 N.E.2d 1039; 1991 Mass. LEXIS 531


October 10, 1991  
November 18, 1991 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on August 2, 1991.

The case was reported by Wilkins, J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, employees of correctional facility, commenced suit against defendant county sheriff, and sought a declaration that portions of the Massachusetts Fiscal Year 1992 Budget Appropriation Act, 1991 Mass. Stat. 138, which transferred control of the penal institution to the county sheriff, violated the Home Rule Amendment, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 7, § 7L.


OVERVIEW: Under the Massachusetts Fiscal Year 1992 Budget Appropriation Act (Budget Act), 1991 Mass. Stat. 138, the control of a penal institution was transferred from the city of Boston to the county sheriff. The employees of the correctional facility (employees) commenced suit and sought a declaration that the portion of the Budget Act that promulgated the transfer was unconstitutional. The employees claimed that the transfer violated the Home Rule Amendment, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 7, § 7L. The court entered judgment in favor of the county sheriff. The court held: (1) the Home Rule Amendment did not preclude the state legislature from acting on matters state, regional, or general concern; (2) the transfer legislation predominately concerned state, regional, and general matters; (3) while the legislation had some special effect on Boston's penal institutions department, the effect neither diminished the Home Rule Amendment's broader purpose or made the Home Rule Amendment applicable; and (4) the Home Rule Amendment did not apply because the legislation provided for funds for the expansion of county correctional facilities and not funds for the payment of expenses of the Commonwealth.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the employee's suit against the county sheriff, which sought a declaration that portions of a state budget appropriations act that transferred control of the penal institution that they worked in to the county sheriff violated a home rule statute.

 

160 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Kelley


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


411 Mass. 212; 581 N.E.2d 472; 1991 Mass. LEXIS 532


September 10, 1991  
November 18, 1991 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on March 25, 1991.

The case was heard by Greaney, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, commonwealth and the Department of Youth Services (Massachusetts), challenged an order of the Supreme Judicial Court for the County of Suffolk (Massachusetts), which denied their petition for relief and discharged defendant from the Department's custody.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with murder when he was 16. He admitted to charges of delinquency and was committed to the Department. The Department ordered defendant's commitment extended based on 1990 Mass. Acts ch. 267, §§ 6-9, which amended Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 120, §§ 16-19. The trial court denied the Commonwealth and Department's petition for relief and discharged defendant. The court held that the change effectuated by 1990 Mass. Acts ch. 267, § 7 could not lawfully be applied to reduce the amount of proof necessary to extend defendant's commitment to the Department. The amendment increased the punishment beyond that which could have been imposed at the time of the offense. 1990 Mass. Acts ch. 267, § 9, which amended Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 120, § 19 by increasing the time period of an extension order to age 21, became an ex post facto law because it was retrospective and more burdensome to defendant. The amendment not only increased the period that defendant could be held in custody to beyond the age of 20 but could bring about his transfer to the adult correctional department for that additional period.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that denied the petition for relief filed by the commonwealth and Department and discharged defendant from the Department's custody.

 

161 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Molino


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Middlesex


411 Mass. 149; 580 N.E.2d 383; 1991 Mass. LEXIS 526


September 10, 1991  
November 4, 1991 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] INDICTMENT found and returned in the Superior Court Department on March 22, 1988.

The case was tried before James D. McDaniel, Jr., J.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the superior court (Massachusetts), which entered judgment on the jury's verdict that found defendant guilty of trafficking in cocaine and of assault and battery on a police officer in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch.. 94C § 32E (1988) and Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 265 § 13D (1990). The court transferred the appeal sua sponte.


OVERVIEW: After his trial on narcotics and assault charges, defendant claimed that the trial judge's restrictions on standby counsel's trial participation were an abuse of discretion that violated his right to a fair trial and to due process. Defendant argued that even though he chose to represent himself, he had a constitutional right to some level of assistance from counsel. The court disagreed, finding that (1) the appointment of standby counsel was within the broad discretion of the trial judge; (2) the trial judge's discretion to appoint or deny the appointment of standby counsel included the discretion to appoint counsel with any reasonable limitations; (3) the strict limitations on counsel's ability to prompt defendant to object, to ask certain questions, or to talk at sidebars were not unreasonable; and (4) the trial judge did not abuse his discretion, nor were defendant's constitutional rights violated by the restrictions. The court held that defendant's sentence was neither illegal nor unconstitutional because it fell within the range permitted by Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 94C § 32E(b)(2) (1988), and there was no evidence that the sentence included punishment for defendant's contempt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

School Committee of Worcester v. Worcester Div. of Juvenile Court Dep't


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


410 Mass. 831; 575 N.E.2d 1120; 1991 Mass. LEXIS 402


April 4, 1991  
August 8, 1991 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on January 2, 1991.

The case was reported by Greaney, J.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, school committee and superintendent of schools, filed a complaint pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 211, § 3 (1990) against defendant juvenile court. The complaint requested a stay of the juvenile court's order requiring the school committee to reinstate a juvenile that had been suspended from school for one year under a school committee policy that the juvenile court had declared unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: In the course of a dispositional hearing on a child in need of services proceeding, the juvenile court declared unconstitutional a school committee policy expelling any high school student bringing a weapon onto school premises. The juvenile court ordered the school committee to reinstate a juvenile who had been suspended for one year in accordance with that policy. Plaintiffs filed a complaint under Mass. Gen. OUTCOME: The court remanded the case to a single justice of the juvenile court. The court instructed that a judgment be entered directing the juvenile court to vacate the portions of its order requiring the school committee to reinstate a juvenile that had been suspended for violation of a school policy and declaring the school policy unconstitutional.

Boston Housing Authority v. Guirola


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


410 Mass. 820; 575 N.E.2d 1100; 1991 Mass. LEXIS 399


April 1, 1991  
August 8, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected October 1, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: CIVIL ACTION commenced in the City of Boston Division of the Housing Court Department on March 13, 1989.

The case was heard by E. George Daher, C.J.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant tenant appealed the decision of the City of Boston Division of the Housing Court Department (Massachusetts), which terminated her tenancy on plaintiff's housing authority's premises after illegal drugs were discovered therein.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, housing authority, brought an action to terminate defendant's tenant's lease after illegal drugs were discovered in her apartment during routine maintenance of the apartment. The trial court awarded judgment in favor of plaintiff, terminating the lease, and defendant appealed. The court affirmed holding that the trial court properly determined that the lease could be terminated because an occupant of the unit used the apartment for unlawful purposes. The court held that U.S. Const. amend. V did not apply where the criminal charges were dismissed due to a lack of evidence because it did not purport to resolve the question of her guilt or innocence. The court concluded that the evidence was properly not suppressed because management was authorized to be there when it provided two written notices before the 48-hour deadline to inform defendant of the scheduled extermination, and where the lease allowed management entry without notice for emergency purposes. The court concluded that the sawed-off shotgun and drugs were left in the apartment in plain view; therefore, defendant's reasonable expectation of privacy in these items was substantially diminished.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment terminating defendant's tenant's lease after plaintiff, housing authority, brought a termination action after drugs were found in defendant's apartment because it was proper for the trial court to order termination when an occupant of the apartment used it for unlawful purposes. The court held that the evidence was admissible where defendant left the items in plain view.

Leibovich v. Antonellis


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Middlesex


410 Mass. 568; 574 N.E.2d 978; 1991 Mass. LEXIS 344


May 7, 1991  
July 3, 1991 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Superior Court Department on February 12, 1987.

The case was tried before James L. Vallely, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant drivers sought review of a decision by a Massachusetts Superior Court, which rendered judgment on a jury verdict awarding appellee parents damages for loss of consortium from injuries sustained by their child in an automobile accident.


OVERVIEW: The parents of an injured child were awarded loss of consortium as an element of damages. The drivers contended that the trial court erred in ruling on the expert witness' qualifications, in denying the requested jury instructions regarding tax consequences, and in retroactively applying the rule permitting loss of consortium. The court held that: (1) the fact that the expert's qualifications were previously laid out, and the lower court allowed the expert's testimony after an objection, clearly implied a determination as to the witness' qualifications; (2) once the lower court had made a preliminary finding as to the expert's qualifications, it was the jury's function to determine the credibility of the expert's testimony; (3) testimony as to the decrease in damage projections due to taxes did not seriously bring the subject of taxes to the jury's attention; (4) the legislature expressly intended the loss of consortium statute to apply retroactively; and (5) retroactive application did not violate the drivers' due process rights because retroactive application was reasonable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment to the parents of damages for loss of consortium from injuries sustained by their child.

German v. Commonwealth


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


410 Mass. 445; 574 N.E.2d 336; 1991 Mass. LEXIS 333


May 9, 1991  
June 18, 1991 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Superior Court Department on April 10, 1991.

The case was reported to the Appeals Court by Elbert Tuttle, J., on a statement of agreed facts. The Supreme Judicial Court transferred the case on its own initiative.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state employee (employee) commenced this action against defendant state in the Superior Court (Massachusetts), which pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 231, §111 reserved and reported the issues presented to the appellate court. The court then transferred the case on its own motion to determine the constitutionality of 1991 Mass. Acts. ch. 6, §90, or the furlough law.


OVERVIEW: The employee filed an action against the state after 1991 Mass. Acts. ch.6, §90, or the furlough law went into effect because based on her salary, she was furloughed for eight days. After the trial court reported the case to the appeals court, the court on its own initiative transferred the case to determine if § 90 was constitutional. The court was asked to decide whether §90 imposed a discretionary and unconstitutional graduated tax on state employees and whether it effected a governmental taking of the employee's property without reasonable compensation in violation of Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights art. 10. The court determined that §90 did not impose a tax on state employees because it did not raise revenue for the state, but was a decrease in expenditures of the state. The court determined that the law did not result in a taking of her property, because the employee had no employment contract for any definite period of time. Therefore, she did not have a property interest in future wages.


OUTCOME: The court found that the statute in question was constitutional in the employee's action against the state.

Kopycinski v. Aserkoff

June 18, 1991

PRIOR HISTORY: CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Superior Court Department on November 20, 1989.

DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, wife of deceased (wife), filed a complaint for medical malpractice against defendants, hospital and doctors. A medical malpractice tribunal (tribunal), convened to review the wife's offer of proof. The tribunal consisted of a physician, an attorney, and a judge of the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts). The attorney and the physician found for each doctor. The judge overruled the majority. The hospital and doctors appealed.


OVERVIEW: The wife's husband went to the hospital's emergency ward complaining of vomiting, inability to eat, and excessive weight loss. A doctor examined him and admitted him to the hospital. Although a CT-Scan showed evidence of an inguinal hernia, the doctors allegedly failed to determine that the hernia was the cause of the decedent's medical problems. Less than twenty-four hours before his death, the doctors obtained a surgical consultation, which recommended an exploratory laparotomy after the decedent's condition was stabilized. The superior court reversed the medical malpractice tribunal's decision and held that the offer of proof was sufficient. The court affirmed, holding that the two panel members erred in deciding that the wife's offer of proof in regard to the three doctors was not sufficient to raise a legitimate question of liability appropriate for judicial inquiry. The wife's offer of proof alleged that the doctors failed to diagnose or treat the hernia, that their treatment of husband fell below the requisite standard of care, and that husband's death was the result.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court judge's decision to overrule the majority of the medical malpractice tribunal as the offer of proof was sufficient for the wife to proceed without posting a bond. Thus, the court remanded.

Globe Newspaper Co. v. Commissioner of Revenue

OVERVIEW: The newspaper company sought a declaration that two new tax amendments, 1990 Mass. Cambridge v. Attorney Gen.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


410 Mass. 165; 571 N.E.2d 386; 1991 Mass. LEXIS 269; 13 Employee Benefits Cas. (BNA) 2588


February 5, 1991  
May 16, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected May 24, 1991. Second Correction July 26, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Superior Court Department on December 20, 1988.

The case was reported to the Appeals Court by J. Owen Todd, J., on a statement of agreed facts. The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct review.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, municipalities and insurer, instituted an action in the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts). At issue was whether statutes mandating the inclusion of certain benefits in all health insurance plans sold in the state violated Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights amend. art. 115. Defendant attorney general asserted counterclaims for enforcement. The trial court granted a motion for a report of the case and direct review was granted.


OVERVIEW: The municipalities purchased group health insurance plans for their employees. The municipalities and insurer sought a declaration that art. 115 permitted them to exclude the following statutorily mandated benefits from their contracts with the insurer: PAP smears and mammography, 1987 Mass. Acts ch. 363; preventive and primary care services for children, 1988 Mass. Acts ch. 23, §§ 48, 52, 60; lead poison screening for children, 1987 Mass. Acts ch. 773; nonprescription enteral formulas for Chrohn's disease and ulcerative colitis, 1987 Mass. Acts ch. 683; diagnosis and treatment of infertility, 1987 Mass. Acts ch. 394; and chiropractic services, 1987 Mass. Acts ch. 711. The court held that art. 115 did not preclude enforcement of the statutes. Article 115 did not limit the legislature's ability to enact laws for the general welfare and generally applicable insurance regulations were not the type of regulation of municipal employment contemplated by the article. The municipalities' provision of group health insurance was voluntary and they accepted the obligation to purchase plans that were subject to generally applicable regulations that might cause the premiums to rise.


OUTCOME: The court declared that the Massachusetts Declaration of Rights did not render ineffective the statutes challenged by the municipalities and insurer.

Steinbergh v. Rent Control Bd.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Middlesex


410 Mass. 160; 571 N.E.2d 15; 1991 Mass. LEXIS 267


March 4, 1991  
May 15, 1991 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Superior Court Department on April 17, 1987.

The case was heard by Robert J. Hallisey, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs sought review of an order of the trial court (Massachusetts), which entered judgment for defendant Rent Control Board of Cambridge. Plaintiffs brought suit pursuant to the judicial review provision of the Cambridge Rent Control Authorizing Act, 1976 Mass. Acts ch. 36, § 10. They contended that a Board regulation that provided different methods of calculating a rate of returns for large and small landlords was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs contended that a regulation allowing a higher interest rate for small-scale landlords than for large-scale landlords violated the due process and equal protection clauses of the Fourteenth Amendment. They contended that the challenged rule was a rate action, which required a higher level of scrutiny. On appeal, the court held that the Board action was a regulation and that it passed constitutional muster because it was rationally related to a legitimate state purpose. Because the board action was of sufficiently general application, it came within the definition of regulation found in Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 30A, § 1 (1988 ed.). It enjoyed a presumption of validity equal to that of a statute. The asserted purpose of the regulation, to ensure quality rental housing at an affordable price, tracked the purpose of the enabling Act. The distinction between large-scale and small-scale landlords was rational because large-scale landlords had less expensive opportunities for financing and therefore could make a profit at the lower interest rate. Because the distinction was related to a legitimate state purpose, assuring affordable housing, the regulation was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment for the Board in plaintiffs' action to declare a Board adopted regulation to be unconstitutional.

 

172 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Fenderson


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Norfolk


410 Mass. 82; 571 N.E.2d 11; 1991 Mass. LEXIS 205


January 10, 1991  
May 9, 1991 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] INDICTMENT found and returned in the Superior Court Department on August 2, 1989.

A pretrial motion to suppress evidence was heard by Robert A. Mulligan, J., and the case was heard by Roger J. Donahue, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court (Massachusetts), which convicted him, without a jury, of trafficking in cocaine in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 94C, § 32E(b)(2) (1988). Defendant argued that the denial of his motion to suppress evidence was an error.


OVERVIEW: Based on information from informants who provided information regarding defendant's trafficking in narcotics and who made supervised purchases from defendant, the police submitted affidavits for a warrant authorizing a wiretap of his telephone. They also obtained a warrant to search his safety deposit boxes. Defendant sought to suppress the evidence. The court found that the explanation in the affidavit that the informants were unwilling to testify for fear of reprisal, the difficulty of visual surveillance, the lack of information obtained from his telephone record, and the probability that the search of his home would be fruitless, supported the reasonableness of the use of electronic means of surveillance techniques. The affidavit furnished sufficient information to show a reasonable likelihood that traditional investigative techniques either failed or would have failed, if attempted, in providing the police with information regarding the defendant's drug-trafficking activities. The affidavit for a warrant to search the safety deposit properly concluded that there was probable cause to believe that the safety deposit box contained evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant of trafficking cocaine.

Morey v. Martha's Vineyard Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


409 Mass. 813; 569 N.E.2d 826; 1991 Mass. LEXIS 195


February 4, 1991  
April 18, 1991 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Superior Court Department on July 31, 1986.

The case was heard by Elbert Tuttle, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On its own motion the court transferred, from the Appeals Court (Massachusetts), the appeal brought by plaintiff property owners from a trial court judgment that had affirmed the decision of defendant commission of Martha's Vineyard that restricted the construction of a guest house on plaintiffs' lot in Edgartown.


OVERVIEW: The commission of Martha's Vineyard had issued a decision that restricted the construction of a guest house on the lot of the property owners in Edgartown. The property owners then filed a complaint in the trial court challenging the commission's decision, which the trial court affirmed in favor of the commission. On appeal by the property owners, the court reversed the trial court's judgment. The court found the commission had lacked jurisdiction under its enabling statute, 1977 Mass. Acts ch. 831, to review a proposed building on the property owners' vacant lot. Specifically, the court found the commission's regulation allowing cross-town referrals was invalid. The commission's enabling statute permitted only the permitting agency in the town where a project was located to refer that project to the commission for review as a development of regional impact. The court concluded that the commission lacked jurisdiction to review the application because it was not referred by Edgartown.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, and reversed the decision of the commission of Martha's Vineyard that restricted the construction of a guest house on the lot of the property owners in Edgartown. The court issued an order that a new judgment should be entered annulling the commission's decision.

Liability Investigative Fund Effort v. Medical Malpractice Joint Underwriting Ass'n


No. Hd-5464


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


409 Mass. 734; 569 N.E.2d 797; 1991 Mass. LEXIS 190


December 3, 1990, Argued  
April 10, 1991, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Hampden.

Civil actions commenced in the Superior Court Department on May 3, 1989 and June 2, 1989, respectively.

In the second case, a motion to dismiss was heard by Raymond R. Cross, J. The cases were then consolidated for trial and were heard by John F. Moriarty, J., on further motions to dismiss.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review as to the first case and on its own initiative transferred the second case from the Appeals Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff physicians sought declaratory and equitable relief in Superior Court (Massachusetts) with regard to malpractice rate increases approved by defendant insurance commissioner under the commissioner's malpractice rate regulations. The trial court dismissed plaintiff's complaint. Plaintiffs sought further review.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff physicians filed actions in superior court seeking declaratory and injunctive relief with regard to medical malpractice rate regulations promulgated by defendant insurance commissioner. The trial judge dismissed plaintiffs' complaints on the basis that exclusive jurisdiction over their claims was vested in the supreme judicial court under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 175A, § 5A. On appeal, the court reversed the dismissal of the complaints in their entirety, and remanded the case for a determination as to which claims required resolution under § 5A. The court held that, under § 6, ratemaking challenges could not be heard by the superior court. The court directed that, on remand, each count of the complaints be examined to determine which required the commissioner's adjudication. The court held that those counts not challenging the substance of a ratemaking decision or which did not otherwise require exhaustion of administrative remedies could be adjudicated in the superior court. The court held that the trial court might wish to stay proceedings to await the outcome of the deficit recoupment proceeding pending before the commissioner.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the superior court dismissing plaintiff physicians' complaints. The court remanded the case to the trial court for a determination of those counts setting forth matters within the authority of the insurance commissioner, and for the issuance of a stay pending the commissioner's resolution of issues related to deficit recoupment.

 

175 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


News Group Boston, Inc. v. Commonwealth


Nos. 5563, 5566


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


409 Mass. 627; 568 N.E.2d 600; 1991 Mass. LEXIS 121; 18 Media L. Rep. 2102


March 7, 1991, Argued  
March 28, 1991, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on February 1, 1991.

The case was heard by Lynch, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the Commonwealth and the juveniles, challenged a judgment from the Supreme Judicial Court, Suffolk County (Massachusetts), which granted plaintiff publisher access to the court proceedings of the juveniles, without prejudice to impoundment, stating that Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 119, § 65 (1990) applied to the juveniles, who were charged with delinquency by reason of murder, aggravated rape, and armed robbery.


OVERVIEW: Admitting the public to the proceedings was procedural, not a change in the juveniles' substantive rights. The court opined that increasing the punishment imposed beyond what could have been imposed would be ex post facto, but opening the proceedings to the public and possibly stigmatizing the juveniles was not punishment in a constitutional sense. The court held that it violated the juveniles' constitutional rights to single them out for treatment different from those who were charged with delinquency by reason of a crime other than murder. The court noted that juveniles did not have a fundamental, due process right to have the public excluded from a transfer hearing, and juveniles charged with murder were not a suspect class for whom a heightened test of the constitutionality of legislation applied; therefore, equal protection principles required only that the amendment was a rational means to serve a legitimate end. The court opined that the legislature had to balance the juveniles' interests and the juvenile justice system against the public's interest in being able to determine whether a decision to transfer a juvenile to adult jurisdiction was lawfully and soundly made.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which granted the publisher access to the court proceedings of the juveniles.

Ram v. Charlton


No. 5484


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


409 Mass. 481; 567 N.E.2d 208; 1991 Mass. LEXIS 101


December 6, 1990, Argued  
March 7, 1991, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Civil action commenced in the Superior Court Department on November 14, 1986.

Motions for summary judgment were heard by Elbert Tuttle, J., and Robert A. Mulligan, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff driver appealed a judgment of the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts), which granted summary judgment to defendants, town and commonwealth, in the driver's action seeking to recover damages for injuries sustained while driving on an allegedly negligently designed road in the town.


OVERVIEW: A driver filed an action against the town and the commonwealth after she sustained injuries in a one-car accident on an allegedly negligently designed town road. The superior court granted summary judgment for the town and the commonwealth holding that the driver failed to give the notice required as a condition precedent to maintaining actions under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 81, § 18 (1988) and Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 84, § 14 (1988). On appeal, the court affirmed summary judgment for the town and the commonwealth. The court held (1) the statutes were exclusive remedies for the driver, (2) the statutes applied because the term "defects" under the statutes is defined in Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 84 as anything in the state or condition of the way that renders it unsafe or inconvenient for ordinary travel, and (3) it was necessary for the driver to comply with the notice provisions of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 81, § 18 (1988) and Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 84, § 14 (1988) because both statutes unequivocally so required.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed summary judgment in favor of the town and the commonwealth.

Ventresco v. Commonwealth


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


409 Mass. 82; 565 N.E.2d 404; 1991 Mass. LEXIS 23


November 5, 1990  
January 9, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected February 6, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on January 18, 1990.

The case was heard by Greaney, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order from the Supreme Judicial Court for the County of Suffolk (Massachusetts), which denied defendant's motion to dismiss the charges of conspiracy, falsifying motor vehicle registration, and conflict of interest.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted on charges of conspiracy, falsifying motor vehicle registrations, and conflict of interest. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss. Defendant also filed a complaint under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 211, § 3. The lower court denied defendant relief and he appealed. The court affirmed. The court stated that a motion to dismiss pursuant to Mass. R. Crim. P. 13 was not appealable by defendant until after trial. Further, the court stated that Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 211, § 3 could not be used to circumvent the rule of procedure. The court stated that defendant failed to meet the two part test in order to obtain pretrial review. The test states that defendant had to demonstrate both a substantial claim of a violation of his substantive rights and irremediable error, such that he could not be placed in status quo in the regular course of appeal. The court stated that defendant's argument that the grand jury lacked neutrality was without merit because there was nothing in the record that in any way impugned the neutrality of the grand jurors. Further, the court stated that defendant made no showing that he had a constitutional right not to be tried.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's ruling that denied defendant's motion to dismiss the charges of conspiracy, falsifying motor vehicle registration, and conflict of interest.

 

179 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Society of Jesus v. Boston Landmarks Com.


No. 5415


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


409 Mass. 38; 564 N.E.2d 571; 1990 Mass. LEXIS 532


November 6, 1990, Argued  
December 31, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended February 11, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Suffolk.

Civil actions commenced in the Superior Court Department on June 10, 1987, August 27, 1987, and November 24, 1987, respectively.

The cases were consolidated for trial and were heard by Elbert Tuttle, J., on a motion for summary judgment.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a city landmarks commission (commission), challenged a judgment of the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts), which held that the commission's designation of elements of the interior of a church as a landmark violated the free exercise clause of the First Amendment, and granted summary judgment in favor of respondent Jesuits.


OVERVIEW: The Jesuits renovated a church, and the commission approved landmark designation for portions of the church's interior. The designation restricted permanent alteration of certain areas of the church. The Jesuits filed a complaint against the commission, contending that the designation violated the free exercise clause of the U.S. Const. amend. I. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the Jesuits. The court affirmed, and held that the designation of the church interior as a landmark violated Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights art. II. Article II protected the right to freely to design interior spaces for religious worship, thus barring the government from regulating changes in such places, provided that no public safety question was presented. The landmark designation of the church interior unconstitutionally restrained religious worship. The conduct the commission attempted to regulate, renovation of the church interior, neither disturbed the public peace nor obstructed the religious worship of nonmembers of the church. Thus, the designation was unconstitutional under art. II.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of the Jesuits.

Commonwealth v. Scott


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Middlesex


408 Mass. 811; 564 N.E.2d 370; 1990 Mass. LEXIS 525


September 5, 1990  
December 17, 1990

The case was tried before John Paul Sullivan, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts), which convicted him of murder in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: A jury rendered a guilty verdict against defendant based on hearing evidence that police found hairs from defendant on the victim's body and the victim's hairs on clothing belonging to defendant. Further, an eyewitness placed defendant around the scene the evening of the crime and an inmate testified defendant made comments regarding his involvement. Defendant appealed based on various contentions. The court found that defendant did not present any evidence during the motion hearing which established that the method of operation of both crimes was similar to warrant admission of other person's involvement. The trial judge did not err in denying defendant investigatory access to the victim of the second assault because he had access to police report. The court held that the two incidents of harassment when combined with the more serious harassment of another woman, was relevant evidence in showing that defendant may have been sexually frustrated. Further, there was sufficient evidence for a rational jury to infer that defendant attempted, but ultimately failed, to penetrate the victim and that defendant based on the cumulative evidence was guilty of first degree murder.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.
