Commonwealth v. Doe


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Norfolk


408 Mass. 764; 563 N.E.2d 1349; 1990 Mass. LEXIS 518


October 2, 1990  
December 10, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected December 31, 1990. As Corrected February 6, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: ADJUDICATION of contempt in the Superior Court Department on November 17, 1989.

The case was heard by Andrew Gill Meyer, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts), which held him in contempt of court for failing to comply with an order that he appear in a lineup sought by the grand jury. Defendant argued that the order violated his constitutional rights under Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights art. 14, to be free from unreasonable searches and seizures.


OVERVIEW: The evidence before the grand jury showed that witnesses saw a man fitting defendant's description near the scene before he sexually assaulted the victim. Other evidence showed that defendant made obscene phone calls to the victim. The police showed the victim's husband pictures of defendant. The husband, who saw the victim's attacker, pointed to defendant's picture. Based on the foregoing, the prosecution asked the grand jury to request an order that defendant appear in a lineup. The superior court held defendant in contempt for refusing to appear in the lineup. On appeal, the court affirmed the superior court's order of contempt and ruled that the order did not violate defendant's constitutional rights. The court ruled that in order to direct a person to appear in a lineup, the superior court had to determine whether there was "reasonable suspicion" that the person subject to the order committed the crime under grand jury investigation. The court determined that the standard satisfied art. 14's requirement that a search and seizure had to be reasonable. The court concluded that the record showed that there was a reasonable basis for ordering defendant to participate in a lineup.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's order of contempt and held that the order that defendant participate in a lineup was lawful.

Commonwealth v. Purdy


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


408 Mass. 681; 562 N.E.2d 1347; 1990 Mass. LEXIS 484


October 2, 1990  
November 27, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] PETITION filed in the Superior Court Department on August 13, 1986.

Motions to dismiss were heard by Robert A. Mulligan, J., and Guy Volterra, J., respectively, and a question of law was reported to the Appeals Court by Volterra, J. The Supreme Judicial Court transferred the case on its own initiative.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, an inmate in a state correctional center, appealed rulings of the Suffolk County Superior Court Department (Massachusetts) denying his motions to dismiss a petition brought by the Commonwealth to commit him as a sexually dangerous person pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 123A, § 6. Though the appeal was filed with a state appellate court, the court transferred the case on its own initiative.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was serving time for assault and battery using a dangerous weapon and was to become eligible for parole in August 1986. In March 1986, the superintendent sought a psychiatric evaluation under § 6 in order to determine defendant was a sexually dangerous person. After a single examiner found that he was sexually dangerous, the Commonwealth petitioned the lower court to determine that defendant should be committed for treatment under § 6. While denying defendant's motions to dismiss, the trial court ultimately ruled that the Commonwealth had not complied with requirements under § 6, and it ordered the process to begin again. Defendant again moved to dismiss, and his motion was again denied. He appealed both denials, but the court affirmed. It held that the Commonwealth had properly applied a version of § 6 in force at the time the original petition was filed; that the application of the earlier version of § 6 to defendant was constitutional and did not violate his equal protection rights; and that a prior determination that the Commonwealth had not complied with § 6 was not tantamount to a finding that defendant was not sexually dangerous and did not bar further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of defendant's motions to dismiss the petition, and it remanded to the superior court with directions to hold further proceedings to determine whether defendant was properly committed for treatment as a sexually dangerous person.

Department of Revenue v. LaFratta


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Middlesex


408 Mass. 688; 562 N.E.2d 1352; 1990 Mass. LEXIS 487


October 4, 1990  
November 27, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Somerville Division of the District Court Department on July 23, 1987.

The case was heard by Henry A. Tempone, J., on a motion to dismiss.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Department of Revenue appealed a judgment from the Somerville Division of the District Court Department (Massachusetts) granted in favor of defendant purported father. The department challenged a dismissal of its paternity and support action filed on behalf of the mother pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 209C.


OVERVIEW: The mother gave birth to a child after having sexual relations with the purported father. The department filed a first criminal complaint against the purported father under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 273, § 12, for a determination of paternity and child support and he made a lump sum payment to the department. The first complaint was dismissed with prejudice. Almost four years later the department filed a second complaint under a successor statute to the repealed ch. 273, Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 209C. The court affirmed the contested judgment because the dismissal with prejudice of the first complaint barred the second complaint. The court held that re-adjudication was precluded by ch. 209C. The court ruled that the dismissal with prejudice of the first criminal complaint was the equivalent of an acquittal of the purported father, which prevented the department from filing the second complaint against him. The court decided that the dismissal of the first complaint with prejudice was a final adjudication under ch. 273. The department was prohibited by the doctrine of separation of powers in the Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights art. 30 from relitigating the issue of paternity and support.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment challenged by the department and entered for the purported father, which dismissed the department's paternity and support action.

Adoption of Alex


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Essex


408 Mass. 522; 562 N.E.2d 78; 1990 Mass. LEXIS 467


September 6, 1990  
November 8, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] PETITION filed in the Essex Division of the Probate and Family Court Department on October 28, 1987.

CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Essex Division of the Probate and Family Court Department on June 1, 1988.

The cases were heard by William Highgas, Jr., J.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant putative father challenged the judgment of the Essex Division of the Probate and Family Court Department (Massachusetts), which dismissed the putative father's paternity complaint and his petition to revoke the adoption of the child by appellee mother and her husband. The father also sought to appeal the order of a single justice of the court which denied the putative father's petition for leave to appeal the judgment of adoption.


OVERVIEW: The putative father argued, inter alia, that Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 210, §§ 2, 4A (1988) were unconstitutional and that the trial court erred in dismissing his complaint for paternity and his petition to revoke the judgment of adoption. The court affirmed, inter alia, the trial court's judgment. The court did not address the constitutionality of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 210, § 2 because the putative father did not pursue his original request of a report to the intermediate appellate court on the issue of its constitutionality. The trial court did not err in dismissing the complaint to establish paternity. It was legally irrelevant whether the putative father was in fact the child's father because his rights, duties, and legal consequences were terminated when the trial court signed the adoption order and because the single justice denied the putative father's petition to for leave to appeal the judgment of adoption. Furthermore, the trial court did not err in denying the putative father's petition to revoke the judgment of adoption because once the court's single justice denied his petition for leave to appeal the adoption, the putative father could not seek to revoke the adoption.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which dismissed the putative father's complaint to establish paternity and petition to revoke the judgment of adoption. The court also affirmed the single justice's order denying the putative father's petition for leave to appeal the adoption.

Commonwealth v. Skinner


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Middlesex


408 Mass. 88; 556 N.E.2d 1014; 1990 Mass. LEXIS 330


April 3, 1990  
July 18, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] INDICTMENT found and returned in the Superior Court Department on July 30, 1985.

The case was tried before Hiller B. Zobel, J., and a motion for a new trial was heard by him.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts), which convicted him of murder in the first-degree. Defendant did not appeal his conviction for unlawfully carrying a firearm. Defendant also appealed a denial of a motion for new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant hired new counsel, and in addition to the appeal of his conviction and the denial of his motion for a new trial, defendant also appealed the denial of his motion for new trial, which was heard by the trial judge on remand. The court consolidated both the appeals. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial judge erred in giving a supplemental instruction in response to a jury question regarding deliberate premeditation. Defense counsel did not object to the supplemental instruction. The court found that the trial judge failed to redefine premeditation. Because the jury's question sought to assistance in exploring the distinction between murder in the first and second degree, the trial judge's silence on premeditation fell short of providing a comprehensible standard to guide them. Based on the supplemental instruction given, the jury could have understood that the Commonwealth was relieved of its burden to prove deliberate premeditation as well as malice, in order for them to return a verdict of murder in the first-degree. Moreover, the judge's main charge to the jury before they retired to deliberate did not cure the flaw of the supplemental instruction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order, which denied defendant's motion for a new trial, reversed and set aside the verdict of murder, and remanded to the superior court for a new trial.

Opinions of Justices to Governor


No. 5425


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


408 Mass. 1201; 556 N.E.2d 1002; 1990 Mass. LEXIS 332



July 17, 1990 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Governor of the Commonwealth of Massachusetts presented the court with an order requesting an advisory opinion regarding House No. 5858, entitled "An Act establishing the economic stability and recovery compact" (Act).


OVERVIEW: The governor had doubts about the constitutionality of certain provisions of the Act and presented a question to the court, pursuant to Mass. Const. Declaration of Rights amend. art. 85. In this advisory opinion, the court stated that it restricted its response to the important, broad issue, implicit in the governor's question of whether the legislature had the authority to impose an excise upon the sale of services enumerated in House No. 5858 as "commodities" pursuant to the taxing power conferred by Mass. Const. Part II, ch. 1, § 1, art. 4. Thus, after a review of the meaning of the word "commodities " in the state constitution, the court answered the question in the affirmative and concluded that once it was appreciated that the word "commodities" in the state constitution was not limited to tangible personal property, but included those benefits, privileges, and activities that could be regulated by the commonwealth, an excise upon the sale of services, as enumerated in House No. 5858, fell within the legislature's authority under the state constitution, provided it was reasonable and was not a property or income tax masquerading as an excise.


OUTCOME: The court concluded that an excise upon the sale of services fell within the legislature's authority under the state constitution, provided it was reasonable and was not a property or income tax masquerading as an excise.

 

188 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Digital Equipment Corp. v. Commissioner of Revenue


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


408 Mass. 18; 556 N.E.2d 371; 1990 Mass. LEXIS 319


March 7, 1990  
July 12, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a decision of the Appellate Tax Board.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayer sought review in the appeals court of the decision of the Appellate Tax Board affirming the tax deficiencies assessed by respondent Commissioner of Revenue. The court, on its own initiative, transferred the case to its own docket. At issue was whether the taxpayer was entitled to job incentive deductions for the wages it paid to certain employees working at its facilities located in impoverished parts of the state.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer obtained certificates of eligibility from the state agency that administered the job incentive program, and claimed deductions for portions of the wages it paid to workers hired at its eligible facilities. The commissioner disallowed a portion of the job incentive deductions and the taxpayer sought review in the Tax Appeals Court, which affirmed the commissioner's decision. The taxpayer sought review. The court held that the commissioner was incorrect in disallowing the deductions for employees residing in communities contiguous to areas eligible for the incentive program because the enabling legislation clearly provided that deductions could be claimed for such employees if they had not moved in the prior year. The court found that a later-enacted statutory cap on the amount of deduction allowed per employee could not be imposed retroactively to employees living in the eligible areas, but held that the cap could be applied to employees domiciled in contiguous areas because in amending the original legislation to permit a deduction for such employees, the legislature created a new category of employees and as to them, the application of the cap was not retroactive.


OUTCOME: The court held that the taxpayer was entitled to the full job incentive deductions it claimed for employees domiciled in municipalities designed as eligible, and held that the taxpayer was entitled to take a deduction, up to the statutory cap, for employees domiciled in contiguous municipalities who had not moved in the prior year. The court remanded for further proceedings consistent with its opinion.

Weld for Governor v. Director of Office of Campaign & Political Finance


No. 5358


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


407 Mass. 761; 556 N.E.2d 21; 1990 Mass. LEXIS 303


May 10, 1990  
July 2, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on April 3, 1990.

The case was reported by Lynch, J. 



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, republican candidates for the offices of governor and lieutenant governor and their respective political committees, brought an action against defendants, the Director of the Office of Campaign and Political Finance and the Attorney General, seeking a declaration regarding joint expenditures made by plaintiffs.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were the state officials empowered to investigate and prosecute alleged violations of the campaign finance laws. Plaintiffs sought a declaration pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 231A (1988), that joint expenditures they had made for the purchase of campaign buttons, bumper stickers, and signs bearing the names of both candidates had not constituted unlawful contributions prohibited by Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 55, § 6 (1988). In the alternative, plaintiffs made state and federal constitutional arguments. Defendants had defined "joint expenditure" as any expenditure that was made in cooperation or consultation with any candidate, or a nonelected political committee organized on behalf of a candidate, or any agent of a candidate, or made in concert with, or at the request or suggestion of, any candidate, or any nonelected political committee organized on behalf of a candidate or agent of such candidate. The court declared that Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 55, § 6 (1988) had not prohibited the expenditures that plaintiffs had made and wished to continue to make because shared expenses, evenly apportioned, were not forbidden contributions due to the type of offices sought by plaintiffs.


OUTCOME: The court declared that plaintiffs had made proper joint expenditures for the purchase of campaign buttons, bumper stickers, and signs, which were not unlawful contributions.

Risk Mgmt. Found. v. Commissioner of Ins.


No. 5216


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


407 Mass. 498; 554 N.E.2d 843; 1990 Mass. LEXIS 214


February 7, 1990  
May 23, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CIVIL ACTIONS commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on March 7, 1989, and March 9, 1989, respectively.

The cases were reported by Greaney, J.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, medical centers (centers) and hospital associations, filed complaints for judicial review challenging a decision of appellee insurance commissioner (commissioner) affirming an interim ruling of a hearing officer that pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 362, § 6 (1975), physicians and hospitals may be liable to the joint underwriting association (JUA) for deficits and recoupments could be made pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 333 (1980).


OVERVIEW: In its annual rate filing, the JUA requested to recoup a deficit that resulted from inadequate malpractice insurance premium rates from all licensed physicians in the commonwealth in accordance with § 6. A hearing officer of the division of insurance issued interim rulings concluding that if a recoupment was ordered, all physicians and hospitals, irrespective of the source of their insurance or indemnity coverage, would be subject to recoupment. The centers and the hospital association filed complaints for judicial review challenging the application of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 333 (1980) to non-JUA insureds. The appellate court remanded the cases ordering judgments affirming the commissioner's decision. The court held (1) the recoupment provisions applied to non-JUA insureds because the word "policyholders" included non-JUA insureds, (2) the recoupment provisions were not an unconstitutional delegation of the power to tax because they bore a substantial relation to the public health, and (3) the recoupment provisions authorized recoupments from hospitals of deficits because nothing in the provisions suggested that they were intended to limit the commissioner's discretion.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the cases to a single justice for the order of entry of judgments affirming the decision of the commissioner.

Brookline v. Governor


No. 5250


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


407 Mass. 377; 553 N.E.2d 1277; 1990 Mass. LEXIS 199


January 11, 1990  
May 14, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected June 4, 1990; Second Correction June 19, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Superior Court Department on August 2, 1989.

The case was reported to the Appeals Court by Richard S. Kelley, J. The Supreme Judicial Court transferred the case on its own initiative.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff municipalities filed an action in superior court against defendant governor and other state officials. A judge reported the case to the appeals court on a statement of agreed facts, and the Supreme Judicial Court (Massachusetts) transferred the case on its own motion. The municipalities sought a declaration as to the propriety of the governor's withholding $ 210 million dollars in local school aid funds appropriated by the legislature.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the governor had no authority under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 29, §§ 9B and 9C (1988) to withhold $ 210 million dollars in local school aid funds, known as chapter 70 aid, appropriated in the fiscal year 1990 budget. The court held that the funds appropriated by the line item in question were not subject to reduction pursuant to § 9C, because the school aid funds appropriated by that line item, and assigned in specific amounts to cities and towns by § 3 of the fiscal year 1990 appropriation act, were not made available to any state agency under the governor's control. On a separate request, the court held that 1989 Mass. Acts ch. 240, § 6 lawfully limited distributions of certain state lottery proceeds to cities and towns during fiscal years 1989 and 1990. In modifying the normal appropriation of lottery funds made by the general laws, the court found that the legislature engaged in a process that directly concerned the appropriation of funds for local aid, but that the municipalities failed to present an adequate basis for judicial action under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 29B. The court directed that judgments be entered consistent with the court's opinion.


OUTCOME: The court directed that judgment enter in superior court declaring that the governor lacked authority under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 29, §§ 9B and 9C to authorize a reduction in the line item 1990 fiscal appropriation procedures reducing the amount of local school aid funds. The court directed the trial court to enter judgment that reduced distributions for cities and towns during fiscal years 1989 and 1990 from state lottery receipts were lawful.

 

192 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Gomes


NO. BR-5186


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Bristol


407 Mass. 206; 552 N.E.2d 101; 1990 Mass. LEXIS 134


January 9, 1990  
April 9, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected June 4, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: COMPLAINT received and sworn to in the New Bedford Division of the District Court Department on May 18, 1988.

Entry of a default was ordered by John A. Markey, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the New Bedford Division of the District Court Department (Massachusetts), which, without a hearing, entered a judgment of default and assessed costs on the default because he failed to pay fines in a timely manner, and which ordered his summary confinement. Defendant also appealed the refusal of the Commonwealth to allow to the default costs to be "worked off" pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 127, § 144 (1988).


OVERVIEW: After defendant failed to timely pay fines that he was assessed after being adjudged guilty of possessing an open container of an alcoholic beverage, a default was entered against him by the district court, costs were assessed against him, and his summary confinement was ordered, without a hearing. Defendant appealed. In remanding the judgment, the court held that the district court improperly assessed costs without a hearing because the assessment could only be made in the case of willful default, which could not be determined without a hearing, thus leaving the district court without any basis for its judgment. The court held, and the Commonwealth agreed, that defendant was entitled to a hearing on the default. The court also held that nothing in Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 276, § 36 permitted the district court judge to incarcerate defendant for his failure to pay the fines without first determining whether defendant had the ability to pay the fine. The court also held, and the Commonwealth agreed, that defendant should have been permitted to "work off" the costs and fines pursuant to Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 127, § 144.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case to the district court for a hearing and further proceedings.

 

193 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Couture


No. 5088


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Middlesex


407 Mass. 178; 552 N.E.2d 538; 1990 Mass. LEXIS 158


December 6, 1989  
April 9, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] COMPLAINT received and sworn to in the Lowell Division of the District Court Department on February 12, 1988.

On appeal to the jury session, a pretrial motion to suppress evidence was heard by Neil J. Colicchio, J.

An application for an interlocutory appeal was allowed by Wilkins, J., in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk and the appeal was reported by him.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sought interlocutory review of an order of the Lowell Division of the District Court Department (Massachusetts), which granted defendant's motion to suppress a handgun which was uncovered during a warrantless search of his motor vehicle.


OVERVIEW: After a convenience store clerk reported that defendant was carrying a handgun, the police stopped defendant, searched his vehicle, and seized the handgun. The district court granted defendant's motion to suppress the handgun. On interlocutory appeal, the court affirmed the district court's order, holding that the police did not have probable cause to search defendant's vehicle. The court further held that there was no evidence that defendant had or was about to engage in criminal activity at the time of the search. The court determined that the fact that defendant had been seen in public with a handgun was not illegal per se because the holding of a valid license was an affirmative defense to prosecution under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 269, § 10(a) (1988) for the carrying of an illegal handgun. Finally, the court held that the stop of the vehicle constituted an illegal seizure within the meaning of the Fourth Amendment because the police did not have a reasonable suspicion of criminal activity to justify the initial stop of defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an order of the district court, which granted defendant's motion to suppress a handgun, which was uncovered during a warrantless search of his motor vehicle.

Westcott v. Westcott


No. Hd-5268


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts


407 Mass. 1002; 551 N.E.2d 1202; 1990 Mass. LEXIS 126



April 4, 1990 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff wife sought review of judgments from the Probate Court in Hampden County (Massachusetts), which dismissed her actions against defendant husband for modification of a prior child support order and a complaint for contempt of the support order.


OVERVIEW: The parties obtained a divorce in Massachusetts, and the divorce decree required compliance with a separation agreement entered into by the parties for the husband to pay child support. Thereafter, both parties moved out of Massachusetts. The wife the filed a complaint for modification of the support order and a complaint for contempt of the support order. The husband moved successfully to dismiss each action for lack of personal jurisdiction over him. The court affirmed the judgments, holding that because the wife no longer resided in the commonwealth and because neither party resided in Massachusetts for one year within the two years before the wife brought her action, the trial court had no jurisdiction under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 223A, § 3(g).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments.

 

195 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Nissan Motor Corp. v. Comm'r of Revenue


No. 5219


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


407 Mass. 153; 552 N.E.2d 84; 1990 Mass. LEXIS 128


February 7, 1990  
April 4, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a decision of the Appellate Tax Board.

The Supreme Judicial Court on its own initiative transferred the case from the Appeals Court.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporation filed applications with defendant Commissioner of Revenue (commissioner) for abatement of corporate excise taxes paid to the state based on sales outside the state. The commissioner held that the applications were not filed in a timely manner. The corporation unsuccessfully sought review by the Appellate Tax Board (Massachusetts). The corporation appealed the denial of its applications.


OVERVIEW: The corporation's applications for abatement of corporate excise taxes paid to Massachusetts for sales in New York were filed after the statute of limitations set forth in Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 62C, § 37 had expired. On appeal, the corporation argued that the court should engraft a discovery rule onto § 37 for seeking an abatement so as to avoid the inequitable result of paying taxes to two states for the same sales. The court affirmed the tax board's decision that the corporation did not comply with § 37. The court further held that the fact that the corporation did not seek abatement within the applicable time period did not render the tax scheme unconstitutional under the Commerce Clause or the Due Process Clause. The court held that while due process required the state to give notice of, and an opportunity to challenge, a tax assessment, the state did not violate due process by requiring recourse to be conditioned on compliance with time limitations. The court further held that the Commerce Clause did not grant immunity to foreign corporations from state taxation that did not directly oppress interstate commerce.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the Appellate Tax Board and held that the statute of repose for abatement proceedings was constitutional as to the commerce clause and the due process clause.

 

196 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Oakes


No. W-4289


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Worcester


407 Mass. 92; 551 N.E.2d 910; 1990 Mass. LEXIS 119


December 7, 1989  
March 20, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] INDICTMENT found and returned in the Superior Court Department on January 9, 1985.

Following review by this court, 401 Mass. 602 (1988), there was a rehearing pursuant to an order of the Supreme Court of the United States.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court had reversed defendant's conviction for taking semi-nude pictures of a 14-year-old girl in violation of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 272, § 29A based on the overbreadth of the statute. After oral argument on appeal, the United States Supreme Court held the overbreadth argument to be moot and remanded to the court for proceedings on the remaining issue, an as-applied federal constitutional attack on the statute.


OVERVIEW: In considering defendant's as-applied federal constitutional attack on the statute, the court held that although defendant raised an as-applied challenge to the statute's constitutionality in a pretrial motion, he failed to preserve it at trial. He neither moved for a finding of not guilty nor asked for limiting jury instructions. The court held that since the issue was not raised before the trial court, defendant waived his right to bring the issue before the court. The court determined that contrary to defendant's argument, his conduct was not pure speech but a mix of conduct and speech. The court ruled that the commonwealth had a freer hand in restricting expressive conduct and that the commonwealth asserted an interest in support of defendant's conviction, protecting minors from exploitation, that was unrelated to the suppression of expression. Thus, the court affirmed defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court convicting defendant for taking semi-nude pictures of a minor child.

 

197 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Davis


No. 5206


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Middlesex


407 Mass. 47; 551 N.E.2d 39; 1990 Mass. LEXIS 113


January 9, 1990  
March 15, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] PETITION filed in the Superior Court Department on December 31, 1986.

The case was heard by Hiller B. Zobel, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision of the Superior Court Department (Massachusetts), which adjudged him a sexually dangerous person (SDP) and committed him to the treatment center at the Massachusetts Correctional Institution at Bridgewater for an indeterminate period of from one day to life.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted on two indictments charging three counts of indecent assault and battery on a child and on one indictment charging open and gross lewdness. While serving his sentence, defendant engaged in inappropriate sexual behavior, even when his personal safety was endangered, by making sexual advances to other prisoners. The lower court adjudged defendant an SDP and committed him to the treatment center. Defendant's petition for review was granted, but the court affirmed the lower court. The court held that the test of defendant's commitment was whether constitutional and statutory minimums had been met and not whether there were optimally different or better ways of doing things. Defendant's rights under Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 123A and the Due Process Clause were not violated by the order committing him to the treatment center. There was clear testimony at the SDP hearing that the treatment center offered professionally supervised programs designed to aid in the rehabilitation of SDPs. Defendant's equal protection claim failed because there was no constitutional requirement that all mental patients in state-run hospitals receive the same rights or care.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court that adjudged defendant a SDP and committed him to the treatment center.

Hartford Acci. & Indem. Co. v. Commissioner of Ins.


No. 5136


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


407 Mass. 23; 551 N.E.2d 502; 1990 Mass. LEXIS 116


November 8, 1989  
March 15, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on July 9, 1987.

Motions for partial summary judgment were heard by Lynch, J.

Upon transfer to the Superior Court Department the case was heard by John L. Murphy, Jr., J., on a motion to dismiss.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted a request for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insurers appealed from an order of the Superior Court Department for the County of Suffolk (Massachusetts), which granted a motion by defendant governing committee to dismiss, for failure to exhaust administrative remedies, the insurers' complaint against the committee and defendant Commissioner of Insurance (commissioner) challenging the constitutionality of Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 175, § 113H (1988 ed.)


OVERVIEW: The insurers filed a complaint seeking an injunction and a declaration that § 113H, as applied to the insurers pursuant to a rule promulgated by the committee, was unconstitutional. The rule in issue contained the formulae for determining each insurer's share of expenses and losses incurred on residual market policies under a scheme for providing motor vehicle liability insurance to applicants who were otherwise unable to obtain insurance. The committee filed a motion to dismiss for failure to exhaust administrative remedies. The superior court granted the motion and dismissed the complaint. The court reversed and held that there was no administrative remedy available to the insurers. The court found that Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 175, § 113H(E) did not authorize an appeal to the commissioner from the committee's promulgation of the rule but only from advisory rulings and decisions with respect to the operation of the rule.The court also found that res judicata did not bar the participation by one insurer who had filed a petition with the commissioner to challenge the validity of the apportionment scheme because the commissioner did not discuss the constitutionality of the rule.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order granting the motion to dismiss and remanded to the superior court for further proceedings.

In re McKnight


No. Br-5141


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Bristol


406 Mass. 787; 550 N.E.2d 856; 1990 Mass. LEXIS 85


October 4, 1989  
March 6, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Bristol Division of the Probate and Family Court Department on February 28, 1986.

Petition filed in the Bristol Division of the Probate and Family Court Department on August 3, 1987.

A motion for a preliminary injunction, filed on February 27, 1989, was heard by Ernest Rotenberg, J.

The Supreme Judicial Court granted requests for direct appellate review.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Department of Mental Retardation sought review of a preliminary injunction issued by the Probate Court (Massachusetts) directing it to pay for the care of an autistic and severely retarded adult at a private, residential facility where the adult had lived and been treated over a period of years.


OVERVIEW: A severely retarded adult sought injunctive relief against the Department of Mental Retardation (department) requiring it to provide a safe and adequate treatment and habilitation program. The probate court issued a preliminary injunction directing the department to pay a private residential facility for the adult's care at the approved rate. The court granted motions for direct appellate review of the department's appeal. The court vacated the preliminary injunction and directed that the motion for such relief should be denied. The court held that the proper procedure for asserting the adult's rights against the department would have been the filing of a separate complaint or the filing of a motion to add the department as a party to an existing guardianship proceeding, alleging the grounds and the nature of the relief sought. The court found that the probate court would have been warranted in entering an injunction directing the department to provide care and protective services to the adult and defining the level of such care and services, as well as where the care would take place.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the preliminary injunction and remanded the case to the probate court. The court directed that, after the adult filed an amended complaint in the existing guardianship proceeding, or filed a separate new complaint, the probate judge could enter a preliminary injunction consistent with the court's opinion, followed by a trial on the merits.

 

200 of 1333 DOCUMENTS


Planned Parenthood League v. Operation Rescue


No. 5212


Supreme Judicial Court of Massachusetts, Suffolk


406 Mass. 701; 550 N.E.2d 1361; 1990 Mass. LEXIS 75


November 9, 1989  
February 22, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CIVIL ACTION commenced in the Supreme Judicial Court for the county of Suffolk on August 11, 1989.

The case was heard by Nolan, J., and, on appeal, was consolidated with a separate proceeding before the full court seeking relief under G. L. c. 211, § 3.



DISPOSITION: So ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff league appealed from an order of a single justice of the Supreme Judicial Court for the County of Suffolk (Massachusetts), which vacated a preliminary injunction that required defendant abortion activists to refrain from interfering with league's abortion activities.


OVERVIEW: A single justice vacated a preliminary injunction that required abortion activists to refrain from trespassing on, or obstructing access to, league's offices or clinics where abortion, counseling, and family planning services were provided. The court ordered reinstatement of the injunction because it represented a proper exercise of the discretion accorded to judges to provide appropriate interlocutory relief. The court held that the preliminary injunction was narrow, carefully tailored, reasonably specific, and did not threaten abortion activists' First Amendment rights. The injunction prohibited only that conduct which, although expressive, was not protected by the First Amendment. Therefore, it was not overbroad. Moreover, the state's interest in imposing the injunction justified the minimal limitations that were placed on abortion activists' expressive activity.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the suspension of the preliminary injunction, and reinstated the injunction until the final disposition of the case or until further order of the court.
